<Content>El Convento - a great place to stay despite the problems Stayed at El Convento for a week in December 2008.Location 鈥?Pretty much unbeatable if you want to stay in the Old City. Three sides of the hotel face onto quiet side streets, so there should not be too much noise from the numerous bars and restaurants near by.Building 鈥?Converted convent with open galleries round a central courtyard, Very attractive but somewhat run down. Loads of character and this makes you feel that you are not an ordinary tourist but part of the Old City 鈥渟cene鈥?br/>Reception etc 鈥?pretty goodRoom 鈥?Classic colonial style with high ceiling. Quite spacious 鈥?but again somewhat run down with odd bits falling off here and there. Air conditioning incredibly noisy and not really powerful enough. Even when turned off there was lots of obtrusive roar from the air conditioning duct Balcony 鈥?too hot to sit out most of the time.Public areas 鈥?great roof terraces with views over the old city and the seas 鈥?probably one of the hotel鈥檚 nicest featureBreakfast 鈥?expensive. Best to have some of the hotel鈥檚 free coffee and go out to one of the local cafes.Staff 鈥?friendly and responsive, but facing an uphill battle keeping the old building running.Food etc. Excellent free coffee and free bottled water available all the time. Free wine and cheese reception on roof terrace in evening really good and great opportunity to meet the other guests. Manager around to greet and chat to guest a really nice touch. Two bar/restaurants on site offer interesting tapas and local cuisine.Overall 鈥?If you are looking for Ritz Carlton levels of comfort don鈥檛 stay here.. However as an authentic place to stay in the old city the El Convento is still hard to beat.

<Author>takojin
<Content>Beware great internet rates during busy weekends We stayed at El Convento in early November over Veteran's Day weekend after booking a queen room with limited view three months in advance. We got a great discount rate online for booking three months in advance and paid a 50% deposit at that time. Therefore we were dismayed to arrive in November and learn we had been moved to a room with double beds. The matter was not adequately handled by the manager on duty, but we moved the second night to the room type we had reserved and enjoyed the balance of our stay.After our return, I emailed a complaint to the manager and was impressed with the manner in which he handled the situation and the prompt response to my complaint. We would have been very satisfied if the same level of concern had been exhibited when we discovered the problem after check-in. The problem should have been acknowledged and handled at check-in rather than left for us to discover, complain about, and then not be resolved to our satisfaction.However, El Convento is a beautiful hotel. The restaurants on-site were some of the best meals we enjoyed in Old San Juan. Cana offers a great lunch value and it's lovely to enjoy tapas and wine on the balcony patio outside El Picoteo. Additionally, the wine and cheese reception is well done and we appreciated the complimentary coffee in the morning. We also enjoyed using the beach facilities at a sister hotel and appreciated the tip from the bellman regarding catching the city bus back to Old San Juan.The only other complaint I have is the quality of the mattresses. The mattresses in both rooms were beginning to sag in the middle and were not especially comfortable given the overall quality of the hotel.I would not dissuade people from staying at El Convento as it is beautiful. I would, however, doublecheck and confirm your room type before arrival, especially if you've gotten a really great rate and might get bumped in favor of those paying more.

<Author>frankie868
<Content>Loved El Convento We stayed at El Convento from 12/27/2008-1/2/2009. Not only is the hotel well run by Efrain Rosa, General Manager, but the entire staff from houskeeping to restaurant personnel, to bellmen, to utility personnel, and last but not least, the front office office staff. Special mention is reserved for Guest Services Supervisor, Judith Gantenbein. We travel quite a bit, and we found her to be the most helpful, pleasant, professional concierge of any hotel we have ever stayed in. Her personal attention to every detail of our trip was over the top. What an asset to El Convento she is. If you go to El Convento, you could communicate with her via e-mail before you get there, so you can get a head start on restaurant reservations, and excursions such as the rain forest and walking tours etc. And now a word about Mr. Rosa, the General Manager. Not only was he visable on New Year's Eve, he greeted the guests and poured champaigne for all of the guests at the daily complementary wine and cheese/fruit get together. We stayed at the Ritz Carlton in Puerto Rico two years ago at this time, and the General Manager did not do this on New Yer's Eve. Additionally, a lovely touch was that every room on New Year's Eve received a complementary bottle of champaigne and two glasses in a decorative ice bucket delivered to each guest room. The room also had a flat panel t.v., radio, and internet service. The rooms are turned down nightly and you receive clean towels twice a day, as well as chocolate placed on the bed . You will not find better service anywhere in Puerto Rico, and the Hotel is central to any place you want to go to in Old San Juan. We also took taxi's to the sister hotel, La Concha several times. La Concha is right on the beach, so between El Convento and La Concha, you have the best of both worlds. Our room (513) was very clean. As you can tell, we will return to El Convento the next time we go back to Puerto Rico.

<Author>udalum
<Content>An Interesting, Historic Hotel My family and I were guests at El Convento for five nights. Our party consisted of my husband, myself, and my twelve year old son. The Room:  We stayed in a Queen Deluxe room (room 321). It was a really nice size, and offered a lot of room to spread out. Next to our room was a ramp, and it backed up to a rather quiet street. There were two queen sized beds in this room. The beds and the linens were very comfortable. The room was nicely decorated with old furnishings, and was quite quaint. Also in the room was a small refrigerator, two Boise radios, a flat-screen t.v., two robes, an ironing board with an iron, an old-looking alarm clock, and a safe. Positive comments about the room: It was comfortable, and really just an intersting place to stay.Small problems: If you are sensitive to noise, the bar that is outside the courtyard of El Convento (and not associated with it) can become noisy. Take a pair of earplugs just in case it gets noisy. The heavy rooms doors take care of most of the sound. I used them only twice. I'm very sensitive to sound, and was not displeased about the noise. The Location:The location of the hotel was wonderful. It is right in Old San Juan, where everything is within walking distance. The hotel is close to one of the biggest forts, and a square that has a grocery, and other interesting places to get snacks. The Staff: There were quite lovely and friendly during the stay. Ask them any questions!The Wine and Cheese Hour:This was between six p.m. and seven p.m., and was a highlight of the trip. There was fresh fruit, wine and cheeses, all at no cost. The cheese and fruit were excellent. I don't drink, so I can't say anthing about the wines. There were a few friendly staff members there that could answer questions about the city. The Restaurant for Breakfast:My son and I dined there once. I had buttermilk pancakes,and my son had the french toast. There were both delicious. I am of the personality that I like to have a super quick breakfast, and a leisurely dinner. I learned quickly that I was much happier grabbing a donut at La Bombonera on Calle San Francisco, and walking around the Old City while eating it. Therefore, I recommend eating breakfast at El Convento if you like a leisurely breakfast.El Picoteo (The tapas restaurant in the hotel):We ate there twice. The food was delicious, and the atmosphere can't be any better. I recommend eating there near the beginning of the trip, because it is convenient if you are a guest in the hotel. The hotel in general: It was a very interesting building, since it used to be an old convent. The architecture is marvelous, and the view of the bay was very pretty from the rooftop lounge. There is an extremely small pool on the roof. It was nice to have, because after a long day, taking a dip in the pool was relaxing. It also allowed us a chance to get some sun. The only annoying part of our stay here was that the hotel was quite full. They were unable to check us in until 5:30 p.m. I would recommend if you are staying here, to be ready with a list of things you would like to see/do in the city, and be prepared to walk around for awhile before you check in. That way, you are are not sitting around waiting for your room. I think if I were prepared for this later check-in time, I would not have been annoyed.

<Author>ctaylo25
<Content>Unique hotel experience Overall a very good place to stay in old san juan. This is a very unique part of the city and this hotel is unlike any other I have ever been to. Very cool property with a large courtyard, multiple bars and restaurants, rooftop veranda with a small pool and hot tub. Service was three stars for four star prices, but the location makes up for that. I was disappointed that they do not have readily available valet parking and charge extra for the service, as navigating the streets of old san juan by car is not an easy task. The rooms are small and housekeeping sometimes takes till the late afternoon to clean your room. Other than those few things I have no complaints. The location and beauty of the surrounding streets makes up for the shortcomings. Overall a very cool experience. I would recommend this hotel for a stay in San Juan and would advise to stay in old san juan as opposed to condado or isla verde if traveling to the area.

<Author>dinnerparty2010
<Content>On business, and I am in love with El Convento A mix between 4-star and local, your room is one of 50+ in an extraordinary, converted convent. The care taken to maintain its beauty and charm is second to none (I saw them varnishing the banisters and polishing the stunning antique furniture). Hospitable, unpretentious, generous, El Convento deserves a Best Of nod amongst leading American hotels to which we've grown accustomed, from the finest Schragar and Hilton properties, to the extraordinarily Ritz Carltons and Four Seasons. All the amenities are the same with the exception of a concierge, including privacy, comfort and elegance. The bed is delicious, and there are no smells to speak of which are notable in old cities and on islands. And the 24-hour, rooftop hot tub, plunge pool and fresh coffee are the icing on the cake. It's a safe, perfect location for romance (especially a much needed escape) and business meetings (a board room, outdoor/indoor library and business center) and has excellent restaurants. You'll never feel like you're on a hotel property...there's a courtyard that shades diners from the beating sun below, while rooms rise 3 floors above it on three sides of the building. You'll feel like you went back in time, though spoiled by the modern offerings. The place was nearly fully booked, and I rarely saw guests except at the nightly wine and cheese reception, most of whom were on vacation, there for a wedding, or on honeymoon. Convinced? I'm a snobby NYer who travels for work regularly, so please don't even consider the Sheraton in the same area but opposite 17-story-high cruise ships and other tourism clutter. You'll get what you bargained for -- literally -- if you do.

<Author>workin'guy
<Content>Great historical hotel This hotel is truly a piece of magificient history - the staff were wonderful, excellent service, the place was very clean, the wine and cheese tea each afternoon a wonderful treat - you can sit on the terrace on watch bats fly about early evening while a piano or band plays in the courtyard. I did find it very expensive though, our room over 300$/night, nice kept room but not very large, and our ocean view , well, we could see the ocean all right, but over top of a group of other , not well-maintained buildings. The pool is a splash pool, I have a living room rug about the same size. I guess I had expected a pool I could do laps in. I loved the hotel itself, the history with it, BEAUTIFUL floors, but i did find the tappas restaurant in the hotel very expensive for such tiny servings, After a 200$ bill for three of us, we went out and got something else to eat to fill up; and the room rate I thought was high for the quality of the room that's all. I did enjoy the stay and thought it was a great place, If you don't mind the price tag - you will enjoy it here.

<Content>Very nice hotel It is a lovely hotel. The staff is quite knowledgeable, especially the managers. Like many hotels I stay in, the shower head was placed at it's highest height, and therefore out of my reach. <Author>Greg187
<Content>Great hotel in a great location Stayed one night last week at the El Convento and it was a great stay. I doubt you could find a hotel with more history or character in all of Old San Juan. Not to mention an ideal location. Staff was very friendly and helpful. The room and ammenities were very nice. As others have noted the plunge pool is small and lounge chairs are limited but it was kept very nicely, has great views and was overall just very enjoyable.The highlight of the stay was the afternoon wine reception. A really nice selection of cheese and wine were served on the terrace with brilliant views of the illuminated cathedral. While we did not have the chance to eat or drink at the hotel restaurants, the tapas bar looked real cool.There was however one slight problem - the air conditioner. In the middle of the night (2AM) my girlfriend and I both woke up on the verge of a sweat (the AC was on the lowest possible setting but clearly not working). We called the desk and someone came up super quickly. However, it was only the desk clerk who was helpful but not qualified to fix the problem. He offered to call the off-site engineer or move us to another room. In the interest of time, we took the other room down the hall but he sort of insisted we take all of our belongings with us. Which, as you can imagine, wasn't too fun at that hour. I'm not sure why we couldn't leave them there until morning. These things do I happen and I understand. However, I was surprised that there was no apology or modest compensation the following morning (like sending morning coffee/breakfast up to the room or a small credit). Aside from the air conditioner it was a great stay and I would highly recommend it. It was convenient to all the historic sites, shopping and dining. After a long day of walking the sites, it was great to have our room so close. After a nap by the pool, a shower, and glass of wine...we were only a few minutes walk from our dinner reservation.Oh but just a reminder - this is not a beach hotel. They have an affiliation with a property about 20 minutes away. But...if you are looking for a true beach front/resort type property, you may wish to look elsewhere.

<Author>BermudaMandy
<Content>Absolutely the best choice for Hotels in San Juan! If you are searching for a place to stay in San Juan, you can stop your searching now and book at this magnificent hotel! After reading all of the reviews, we decided to trust tripadvisor and book this hotel and we could not be happier about our choice. I could not possibly describe what a wonderful place this is with words, but I will try. From the moment you walk in the front doors of the hotel, you feel at home. The doorman greets you and sends you on to the concierge. While checking in, the staff is extremely friendly and helpful. They gave us suggestions of what to do around the area, where to eat, what beach to visit, and a map of the area. El Convento is not on the beach, but it has a sister hotel, La Concha that is. Just take a cab over to the sister hotel and you can use their beach chairs, towels, and pool for free!The room was large and the bathroom looked clean and updated. The room had a flat screen TV, hair dryer, radio, shampoo, conditioner, lotion and mouthwash. On the 3rd floor of the hotel, they offered free bottled water anytime you wanted it. This is great to have when walking around downtown or going over to the beach for the day. The wine and cheese hour was amazing! For one hour, you get to mingle with fellow guests and enjoy red wine, white wine, and a variety of delicious cheeses and grapes. The location of the hotel cannot be beat. It is in Old San Juan within walking distance to El Morro (the fort) and a lot of shopping, restaurants, and bars. We found all of the people in San Juan to be very friendly and welcoming also. We were very impressed with how fluently everyone we encountered spoke both Spanish and English. We felt very safe walking around during the day as well as at night. I have stayed at another hotel in San Juan and did not enjoy my stay nearly as much as I did this time. The atmosphere, amazing attentive helpful friendly staff members, and location of this hotel make this hotel number 1 for a reason. I can't wait to go back for a much longer stay in the future.

<Author>Tearitup
<Content>Fabulous Hotel We stayed at the Hotel El Convento for 7 days in September. I loved everything about the hotel. We were treated wonderfully by the staff. Soledad specifically went above and beyond to help us with tour bookings and other things before we even arrived. While the pool area is small as some have said, it is a beautiful oasis in the midst of Old San Juan. We enjoyed sitting in the hot tub in the evening, very peaceful. One of the things we enjoyed the most was that most everything is within walking distance of the hotel. We even walked to the cruise ship docks and took the free ferry across to where the Bacardi factory is located. We much preferred the local Don Q rum though. The staff is really great. We never had a problem with our room being cleaned. Each day when we were out our beds were made, fresh towels and toiletries were left and the drapes were opened to let in the sun. At night, again while we were out, the beds were turned down, chocolates left on the pillows and soft music tuned in on the Bose radio. Very nice service and never intrusive . If you do stay at the hotel be sure to stop by the manager鈥檚 reception held nightly from 6-7pm. A nice variety of wines and cheeses are provided and it鈥檚 a good opportunity to meet some of the other guests. There is library on the third floor where besides a small selection of books and newspapers you will also find a public internet terminal. This comes in handy for checking email (if you must!) and printing out boarding passes and checking flight status. Overall we would highly recommend this hotel. It鈥檚 a beautiful boutique hotel in a unique location.

<Author>bardfan75
<Content>Loved El Convento My sister and I spent two nights at El Convento on a trip to celebrate her birthday. The hotel is old-fashioned and elegant, but not glitzy, which is what I like. It reminded me of European hotels. Because we were there in the off season, we found a rate of $125/night on the hotel鈥檚 website, a bargain compared to the high season rates. The hotel is in walking distance of all the major sites of the city. I recommend this hotel for travelers who want total immersion into the charms of Old San Juan. I do not recommend it for anyone who wants a new building on the beach with big rooms, Jacuzzi tubs, a casino, dancing, etc.The hotel is built around an open courtyard, featuring a restaurant surrounding a large old Nispero tree. Instead of hallways, rooms open on to galleries overlooking the courtyard. Outside each room is a small table and chairs overlooking the courtyard. Our room was small, but had old-fashioned charm鈥攚rought-iron headboards for the beds and antique furniture. A full鈥搇ength window at one end offered a view of a small street below and in the distance, the Atlantic Ocean.A plus was an area with a refrigerator, stocked with free bottled water, and complimentary terry-cloth robes. An honor bar with drinks and snacks was on a terrace downstairs. Tea and coffee were complimentary. At 6 pm, a free reception offered a number of kinds of wine, plus cheeses and fruit. We enjoyed talking to fellow guests at the reception.The pool is small, but the view of the cathedral from the upper terrace is spectacular. There is also a hot tub. We ate at El Picateo, the El Convento restaurant that specializes in tapas. Our server recommended empanadillas filled with lobster to go with the pina coladas we had been craving. They were scrumptious and started us off on a week in which everything we ate was delicious.My only complaint was the $20 resort fee charged on top of the room rates. We arrived after 10 pm the first night so I asked that it be waived since we did not take advantage of any resort features, such as the option to get a pass to a sister hotel on the beach. However, we still had to pay it.

<Author>Jmraggs
<Content>Nice relaxing place in center of town We stayed here several days as a pre-cruise hotel so we could relax and see the city before embarking on our cruise. Since the moment we arrived, the staff was extremely friendly and helpful.Check in was fast and we quickly went to our room on the 5th floor via the elevator. The room was fairly large and very nice with a view to the pool deck area and the San Juan Bay in the distance. We had a queen bedroom which had a nice flat screen TV, nice stereo that sounded fantastic and a desk area. There is ample room in the closet but we couldn't find a safe even though the hotel indicated that there was one. I didn't even inquire as it wasn't a big deal for us.The bathroom was nicely done, not huge but not small either as there was plenty of room for us. The hotel was very quiet and it seemed like we were the only ones there. The outside courtyard is beautiful and hardly used by anyone. We found the food prices at the restaurants a little on the pricey side and that's why I think that not many people were there dining. We did eat at the street level restaurant with patio area which I think was called Cana but I am not sure that was the name. The food was excellent but a little on the pricey side ($10 for our appetizer) but we enjoyed the food at least. The drinks we ordered didn't show up until we were almost finished with our meal even though there were only two other tables of people in the place. The staff seemed a little confused on what drink to make and who requested it. When we finally received our Martinis, but they weren't even what we ordered as far as the flavor, but we just drank them anyway as we didn't want to wait anymore since our meal had now finished.The hotel staff was extremely helpful with suggestions on where to go for local flavor dining in the area where locals dine. They were correct in all of their suggestions. We dined at some great local places.The wine and cheese reception was very good, nice selection of wines and cheeses. We tried the pool and spa a few times just to unwind and it was very enjoyable and a good way to cool off.I would stay here again because it's very close to everything in the center of town but in a very quiet area and the staff was exceptional in friendliness and helpfulness.

<Author>BVIpost
<Content>Amazing boutique hotel We stayed at the hotel between 12 - 14 September 2008. The hotel itself is fantastic - it is steeped in history and the rooms are characterful and clean. The beds are amazingly comfortable. We were on the second floor facing the external courtyard to the front of the hotel and it was incredibly quiet.We ate dinner at the hotel restaurant the first night of our stay. The food was excellent, as was the service. The mojitos from the bar are the best I've ever tasted! The tapas was great - pretty big portions so no need to go too crazy on the ordering (like we did!). I didn't think it was a bad price for the quality/quantity provided. The atmosphere was great and there was even some flamenco dancing on the bar.We went to Hacienda Caribali on the Saturday with friends - 2 of us were horse riding and 2 were going on the quad bikes. We had a fantastic time. The horses are all in great shape. They match the horse to your ability and my horse was responsive, well fed and well behaved. The stables are very clean and well maintained and the horses that were waiting to go on the trail rides were kept together, in the shade with fans blowing on them to keep them cool - they were cooler than we were! I'm happy to recommend this trip to anyone.The quad bike rides were also thoroughly enjoyed and the guides were excellent. The quad bike guide was full of interesting facts about the rainforest and its history.About half way through the trip we all met up together at the river so that the horses could have a break in the shade and we could go for a swim which was great fun.The hacienda is about an hour long drive out of Old San Juan. A representative from the Hacienda arrived around an hour and a half before our trip to collect us from the hotel. She was polite and knowledgable and there were refreshments waiting in the car for us. The taxi ride was complimentary within the trail ride price (which I think is very reasonably priced). We were taken to the hacienda and when we were finished riding we could take as long as we wanted at the ranch before our driver took us back to the hotel, via a different route so that we could see the coast and the famous strip of roadside restaurants.All in all our trip was fantastic and I will definitely be returning to do it again in the coming months. We will be staying at El Convento again - great location, great food and wonderful rooms.

<Author>Blockster
<Content>My new favorite hotel My husband, 20 YO son, and I just came back from a four night stay in Old San Juan, at the Hotel El Convento, September 1-5. It is my new favorite hotel and the ultimate romantic experience. The rooms were gorgeous. We were on the fifth floor, with a view of the harbor, tile floors, a very comfortable bed, and every amenity. The decor is in the Spanish style. Unlike what was posted previously, we found our rooms to be immaculately clean. The housekeeping staff provided turndown service each evening. Not just opening up the bed and putting out chocolates (which were yummy), but the Bose radio was set on classical music, the wet towels were exchanged for new ones and the bathroom cleaned, a bathrobe was placed across the bed, the toiletries were replenished and more bottle water (which is free) was placed in the refrigerator. Perfection.The entire staff was very accomodating. Special kudos to Jaime (AKA James, Jim), the doorman (though we think we got a promotion while we were there. Congrats!). He was so warm and friendly, remembering our names and giving us excellent recommendations when we asked questions. The men and women behind the desk were always pleasant and available to share a map, answer a question, or make arrangements for touring the rainforest. AND the resident cat was often available to accept a head scratching.The wine and cheese reception at 6 each evening was a lovely event, which we attended twice. A large selection of wines, cheeses, crackers and fruit were available, along with the ubiquitous bottled water. And I could purchase my personal vice, Diet Coke. There are candlelit tables, inside and out, and a hostess to faciltate.BTW, the location is perfect for taking off by foot to tour Old San Juan. Please go to my forum posting if you are interested in a summary of our trip.

<Author>CuatroPaisanas
<Content>Fabulous Stay We stayed at El Convento for two nights last week and were certainly not disappointed. It is very romantic, beautiful and steeped in history. The rooms are a little small, but more than comfortable. Rooms include a sound proof door to keep out the noise at night from the many events and special occasions held at the hotel. The concierge arranged a fabulous in room massage for me and my husband. The Tapas restaurant in the hotel is excellent as well. It featured live music both Friday and Saturday night. There is a cozy library where you can read or check email, plus many different verandas or patios with georgous views of the city to sit and relax comfortably out of doors. El Convento is located right in the middle of Old San Juan so it is an easy walk to all the shops, restaurants, and attractions. If you want beach access, they have a sister property in Condado where you can go and enjoy the water. We highly reccomend staying here.

<Author>ericinatlanta
<Content>Old World Charm in the heart of Old San Juan Hotel El Convento is a charming boutique hotel in the heart of Old San Juan, one of the most enchanting cities I've had the opportunity to visit. In the heart of the best of San Juan's best dining, shopping, and siteseeing district, it makes up for the lack of beach access by giving you passes to one of its several sister properties with oceanfront beach access. The hotel employees were extremely helpful in arranging activities, booking services and providing area recommendations and directions, and the hotel is everything one could hope for in the city - beautiful views, gorgeous decor, a beautiful courtyard and a few charming resident cats to greet you at the elevator every night. The nightly wine and cheese reception is an added bonus. Overall - one of our favorite hotels we've ever stayed at. Very highly recommended. If you're considering a visit to San Juan, I'd recommend you stay nowhere else... in talking to the many people we met during our trip, El Convento is everything (location, charm, ambience) that all of the big resorts lack.

<Author>bpharo
<Content>El Convento Hotel in old San Juan was Incredible I choose to spend 2 nights at this hotel to celebrate my sisters 50th wedding anniversary and pre cruise. I wanted something unique and memorable and that is exactly want I got. We took a taxi from the airport which cost 23.00 for 4 people including all of our luggage. When we pulled up to El Convento Feliciano was there waiting for us as if he knew we were coming. He made us feel so special that we will never forget him. From the minute we arrived we were in awe of the hotel. A few months prior to arriving I had requested rooms 216 and 218 because they have actual step out patios. I knew that there was no guarantee that I would get these rooms just because I requested them but much to my surprise I receved an email from the manager himself telling me he would try to accomadate my request and was looking forward to our arrival. This was totally unexpected and appreciated. I was so impressed that the manager would take time to send this email. Melody checked us in, she was so sweet and helpful. Much to my surprise we did get rooms 216 and 218. We had arrived early about 1:30 pm and 1 room was ready and the other room was almost done so Feliciano took our luggage up to the room that was ready and told us about all the ammenities. We sat in the courtyard and had the best sangrias I have every had. What a peaceful feeling we had sitting in this beautiful courtyard, an unforgetable way to start our vacation.The other room was ready within 45 minutes of our arrival. Check in was not until 3PM so we were very excited to get into our rooms early. Our rooms were just as I thought they would be very unique and I am sure with much history. I loved the fact that you could open the outer door for more light and there was an inner glass door to keep out any bugs from the outside. Our bed was comfortable and we had a beautiful patio that had 2 chairs and a table on it, very private. Complimentary bottles of water included daily and a nice flat screen TV. When you walked out of your room there were table and chairs to sit at that over looked the courtyard.Really enjoyed the free wine,cheese and fruit reception nightly at 6pm and the 24 hr coffee and tea on the 4th floor terrace as well as the honor bar, what a great idea and it was well stocked.The roof top terrace was a nice surprise, a great place to relax. My sister has not stopped talking about her 50th anniversary at thia amazing hotel and the hospiality we received. Great Location, 4 great restaurants and a very unique hotel. I am a travel agent and would not hesitate to recommend this hotel. My only regret is that I did not get to meet the manager, well next time because I will be back. By the way try the El Buren restaurant across the street also great food and drinks reasonably priced. Ask for Mohammed the bar tender. He is very special and makes great drinksThanks for the memories Barbara Pharo Tampa Fl.

<Content>Great Location We just returned from Puerto Rico last week and because tripadvisor reviews were such a great help to me during planning, I thought I would do my part and write a review. The alley view from our room was nice and the staff, including the parking valets, were super friendly and knowledgeable. The 24 hour water, tea, coffee service was nice as was the wine/cheese reception every day at 6pm. All in all it is a nice hotel but was not my favorite of the trip.

<Content>Would visit again Overall this place was great! <Author>Tink1234
<Content>charming I couldn't have been happier with our one night stay in June. We had spent the previous 5 days at the Wyndham Rio Mar but we wanted one night in San Juan in order to see the city more fully. We had not originally booked here only b/o the two night minimum on weekends and instead reserved the Marriott in Condado instead, even though honestly, we would have preferred this hotel. Unbeknownst to me, that Marriott was the old Dupont Plaza where the tragic fire of 1986 took place. We had been booked at that hotel for arrival the day of the fire in '86 (when I was but a teenager) and the only reason we were not there was our flight was delayed. To put it mildly, we feel it was a miracle we were not there at the exact time of the fire where 97people lost their lives. Anyway, I found this out only the morning we were supposed to check into the Marriott and I will give them credit, I explained my story and they cancelled our reservation without penalty. I was then scrambling for a hotel and Carlos at El Convento worked a small miracle for us. He found us a double room and waived the 2 night minimum since we were calling for a room for that day. I can't tell you how much his effort and hospitality meant to us.The hotel itself simply could not be more atmospheric and the location was ideal. The nightly wine and cheese reception was a treat with a gorgeous assortment of cheeses and interesting wines, all served on the 4th floor terrace. The 24 hour coffee and tea service and the rooftop pool overlooking the cathedral were also big hits for us. Our room, though without a view, was enormous! All we had to do to get a view was walk 5 paces, so no complaints there. My only word of advice would be for travelers with children. The hotel staff themselves were nothing but gracious and welcoming but I would not say the same for all of the guests - I understand this to a certain point, it is more of an adult hotel but the fact is, they allow children so if other patrons want absolutely no children, they need to find an adult only hotel. We have 2 children ages 5 and 10, who are seasoned travelers and know when they are to be on best manners, and still we got some dirty looks. So while I wouldn't steer families away from the hotel, one night was just right for us. The four of us also had dinner at El Picoteo and thought the food and the atmosphere could not have been beat. I would recommend this hotel for everyone who wants to have total immersion into the charms of Old San Juan, even those with children. I asked my kids to be respectful that the guests were mostly adults who didn't want to hear a lot of screaming kids, and made sure that they were on their best behavior but after that I just didn't let the other guests spoil what is an unforgettable hotel!  
<Date>Jun 30, 2008

<Author>fbusa
<Content>Great place to stay in San Juan If you like small hotels, in central locations, with bags of character and history, an outdoor dining terrace and bar area overlooking the old town square then you will probably like El Convento. If you like big, modern with a casino then this isnt for you.Maybe the hotel overplays the rooms with views and some reviewers have been disappointed - all I can say is that San Juan has mainly flat-roofed buildings with satellite dishes etc. From our room you could technically see the sea but the foreground is the quirky, characteristic roofs - charming in a San Juan way.I loved El Convento for its pretty courtyard, old architecture, the wine and cheese hour on the terrace, a quiet late night drink over-looking the old town square and floodlit church, easy stroll to the water..San Juan is interesting and the bars great fun ! and 2-3 nights about right if just doing the tourist stuff. (if you are a small quiet hotel-type person I would also recommend the Horned Dorset Hotel, Rincon vs the other large Puerto Rican hotels).

<Author>mlc00
<Content>Could have been better We stayed here for 3 nights during our honeymoon. The hotel is in a great location and is a beautiful building. However they seem to rely on their historic hotel designation way too much, as the hotel is very expensive but the rooms and management leave a lot to be desired. The management was not very helpful when we encountered a problem with our room. Also, housekeeping does a subpar job - i don't think they clean the toilets very frequently.We were in a queen deluxe room for $300 (plus tax), although that was the smallest queen bed i have ever seen and my husband and i couldn't fit in the bathroom together (and we are fairly slender people). The first room we were in, which I was told no less than 75 times was their model room (i still have no idea why), had this extremely annoying banging noise coming out of the AC duct that happened every 30 seconds or so (with the AC on or off). We complained that night, were told they had no rooms in our rate, so to check back tomorrow. The banging continued all night, so we complained again the next morning and were told they would send an engineer to look at it and if they couldn't fix it we could switch rooms. When we checked back at 5pm, we were told that the engineer sat in the room for 30 minutes and never heard it. The manager acted liked we were making it up, which is always a nice attitude. She told us that if we still heard it when we went back, she would switch our room. Of course, within 1 minute of being in the room, we heard it. After making the manager and their engineer come to the room with us, they also heard it within a minute or 2. Then the engineer said Yeah, I have heard that before, just not today. And you didn't try to fix it last time? Excellent work ethic. They did switch us to another room, which was very quiet. Upon checkout, when we saw that we were billed the full rate for the first night, we complained to the manager on duty (same one as before, lucky us). We didn't want the room for free, but considering the aggravation I felt a little customer coddling was in order. She was clearly annoyed that we were bothering her again and before I even completed my sentence she said she would give us 30% off the rate. That's all I wanted. Well, with a little less attitude. Bottom line - its a very unique building with a gorgeous patio inside (excellent breakfast at their restaurant), and they have a complimentary wine/cheese thing which was lovely, but the management and housekeeping could use some serious work. It was certainly not terrible, but was far from stellar and its WAY too expensive considering the problems, no matter how much free cheese you give me.

<Content>What a great hotel! The El Convento was highly recommended by friends and also by Trip Advisor so we felt pretty confidentant in our choice of hotel. I have to say, it was a pleasure staying there. In addition to the beauty of the hotel itself, these little things made the stay highly enjoyable: 1) Free internet in the rooms. 2) complimentary bottled water in the in-room fridge and 3) complimentary nightly wine and cheese hour which also included water, coffee, tea, soft drinks, beer, and mixed drinks. The wine choices were excellent as well, 4 different reds and 4 different whites. This area also had complimentary coffee, tea and bottled water all day. I found it so refreshing to not have to pay for an internet connection and also to not get charged $6.00 for a bottle of water like is often the case in many hotels.The other great plus is the location of El Convento, right in the heart of Old San Juan and walking distance to great shopping and dining as well as the forts.

<Author>SarahASeattle
<Content>Charming We stayed at this hotel for an overnight layover on our way to Antigua and it was such a great place! The rooms were very large and clean and beautiful. The hotel had such a charming feel about it that it is a challenge to capture it in words. Cute bar, great little courtyard area that was incredibly picturesque and located in a great part of town for walking the shops and cafes. We felt completely safe here and took advantage of our afternoon to check out what we could of the area. Admittedly we were kind of sad to leave and head to the island, we will definitely stay here again. All of this and it was a really good price as well. It was within good proximity to the airport, maybe a 20 minute cab ride. I highly recommend this hotel. Relatively small and intimate, doesn't feel like those large boiler plate chain hotels. Charming.

<Author>mjack1997
<Content>Beautiful hotel, terrible houskeeping! We have just returned from a 7 night caribbean cruise and decided to stay in San Juan 1 night post cruise. We chose El Convento based on Tripadvisor's review and the location in Old San Juan. Booked the hotel online for $220/night (twin superior). With taxes and fees, the charge was shy of $300.00. So this is not a cheap hotel. Called the hotel a few times to confirm the details of my reservations and requests I made. We requested for an early check in, a late check out and a roll away bed, as there were 3 of us traveling. We got to the hotel around 10:00 am. The hotel was beatutiful, has the elegant old world charm of Spanish colonial times. And being that it is a small hotel, it has the homey feel of a large mansion. The ladies at the front office/reception were very nice. We were told that our room was not ready as it was still occupied and need to be cleaned and should be ready by noon. At this time, I have mentioned my request for the rollaway bed (1st request). I was told it will be taken care of. So we put our luggages in the holding area and went to the courtyard which was lovely and had drinks and we were admiring the hotel architecture. The bartender and the concierge at the courtyard restaurant were very welcoming. I went back to the reception around 11:00 to check if the room was ready, it was not. So we went out to lunch and came back around 1:30 and we were able to get into a room. The room was beautiful, spacious and had a nice view of the cobble stoned streets below. The bathroom was clean but noticed that there was no extra roll of toilet paper (there were 3 of us in the room). And no rollaway bed. I went outside our room to ask the housekeeper we saw in the hallway for a rollaway bed (2nd time). He said, I must let the reception know, which I have already done so. Meanwhile, my cousin just realized that she left a bag at the port. She called reception ASAP and a lady named Christine helped her right away, called the cruiseline and the 'lost and found' at the port. We thought that was really great. On our way out to pick up my cousin's bag and walk around Old San Juan, we stopped by reception to thank Christine and mentioned the rollaway bed (3rd time). Came back to the hotel around 6:00 and enjoyed their complimentary wine and cheese hour. Went to our room and again, no roll away bed. Rested for awhile and headed back out to look for a place to eat, went back to reception and asked to reccommendation. They were very helpful and pleasant. I mentioned that there was no rollaway bed (4th time). This time, the lady asked me if I want it at that moment. I said not really, since we were on our way out to dinner but would like to have it placed in the room when we get back. Got back around 9:30 10:00 pm , and guess what? No rollaway bed. Now I'm annoyed, called the reception right away (5th time) and even they were surprised that at this point in time, there's still no rollaway bed. Since we we exhausted from the day's activities, I just wanted to lie down. I pulled the bed covers and first thing I noticed was the bed sheets did not look fresh and clean. I grabbed the pillow and I was just shocked, the pillow case had stain on it. In my mind, this could not be for a supposedly small luxury hotel. I called housekeeping, a lady answered and told her about the sheets and pillow case. I even asked her to come see it for herself. Meanwhile the housekeeper came with the rollaway and the first thing he said to us was 'it was not my fault', not very professional, I thought. I then showed him the bed sheets and pillow case and asked him if he thinks they were clean? And of course, after he saw the stain on the pillow, he had no response. A lady supervisor came and explained that it was cleaned last night. Of course, they were cleaned the night before for the previous guests, but they were not replaced for the next guests (us) after the previous guests checked out. She did apologize, but I thought it was a stupid excuse. She left, and a houskeeper came back with 1 sheet set, and asked me if I want the other beds changed too? Of course, we do. Then, another housekeeper came with the extra sheets and another guy who seem be wearing a security uniform which I thought was weird. He did not do anything but stood at one corner, while the housekeepers were changing the beds. I even asked the housekeeper, if that was his bodyguard? He did not respond. We got up the next morning, and one by one we showered. As the 3rd person showered, the bath tub was clogged and now we run out of toilet paper. I don't remember whether I called housekeeping about the clogged tub and the toilet paper or if I mentioned it to the receptionist on our way out to breakfast? But nevertherless, they fixed the tub and gave us 1 extra roll of paper which was placed on the table instead of replacing the empty roll in the bathroom. I know that is a minor detail, but it they claim that they are a small luxury hotel, small detail like that is what makes a luxury hotel stand miles apart from the big chain hotels.The hotel is beautiful and the location is really great. I'm not quite sure if I will stay there again. Not so much for the numerous times we requested for a rollaway bed, but really more importanly, about the stained pillow case and used bed sheets. The rest of the staff were very professional and welcoming. Housekeeping really needs help.

<Author>ISeaGreen
<Content>Beautiful hotel, horrible management My brother and I stayed here for two nights at the start of spring vacation. We flew into San Juan, stayed at the Hotel El Convento, then drove to Rincon and spent a week there. The hotel is beautiful. It is very well maintained, and we were very comfortable. I use a wheelchair, so we stayed in Room 501, which is their accessible room. It worked very well for us-it was kind of crowded with the bed and the rollaway, but it was a beautiful room, there was a lovely view, and the bathroom was indeed accessible. Accessibility was iffy in the rest of the hotel-if you are traveling with someone, as I was, no problem. To get to the restaurant, we had to navigate a steep step. Coming into the hotel, there is a very steep ramp that I was unable to navigate on my own. But the staff seemed very kind and helpful (Jaime was very nice).However, a really serious customer service issue arose. I had decided to rent a beach wheelchair to use during my trip and I found a rental company able to supply such a chair. They asked if the Hotel El Convento would be willing to serve as the drop-off/pick-up point for the chair-the company would drop the chair at the hotel, we would pick it up and take it with us to Rincon, then at the end of our trip we would leave it at the hotel for the rental company to pick-up. I sent email to the hotel, and Carlos J. Gomez replied: There will be no problem in receiving the wheelchair from the rental company. Our guest services staff has been alerted to its delivery on the 4th, and it will be safely stored until you need it. The same would apply on the 12th. After you drop it off, we shall keep it stored safely until it is picked up. When we checked out on Sunday, April 6, my brother asked at the front desk regarding the beach wheelchair. He was told that it had not been delivered. I thought there must have been some misunderstanding, so I went to the front desk to inquire. I was told with certainty that no beach wheelchair had been delivered to the hotel. When I seemed doubtful that she understood and tried to explain further, the woman at the desk stated There is nothing like that here, and I would be the one to know. I was hugely disappointed,but it was Sunday, and I didn't have the contact information of the rental company with me. So I decided to try to have the best time I could under the circumstances.When I returned to work Monday, April 14, I contacted the rental company, expressing my disappointment at the misunderstanding. The person who'd helped me with the rental told me that the beach wheelchair was indeed delivered to the hotel on April 4. She also said that it was a brand-new chair, but when it was picked up on April 12, there was sand on it-so someone had used it. Since I'd paid $395 for the rental, I forwarded her email to the hotel, attached my copy of the invoice, and very politely made it clear that I expected them to reimburse me. I sent that message first thing Tuesday morning. When I still had not received any response by Friday, I sent the same message again, adding that if I didn't hear back I would file a complaint with the Better Business Bureau of Puerto Rico; and whether the matter was resolved to my satisfaction or not, I would be posting my experience on TripAdvisor. Finally, Judith Gantenbein contacted me to apologize for the inconvenience of not having the beach wheel chair available. Her email said, My reason to call you via phone today was simply to tell you that we did receive your previous e-mail and that we are working on the solution to come to an agreement with you. Inquires to find out what had happened took a little longer then I anticipated. And I apologize for this delay as well. I will be contacting you via e-mail soon. Should you have any additional questions, please do not hesitate to contact us. I was amazed. I really am not the kind of person who always complains about customer service, I have worked in customer service and it's rough. But this was truly amazing to me. I waited two more days, then I sent them a note to say that they really needed to reimburse me immediately. Finally, a week after my initial request, Carlos Gomez responded, agreeing to reimburse me and apologizing for the delay, saying that they were really busy, but he knew it was no excuse. He also said that he would like to take me to lunch the next time I found myself in San Juan! I decided to let it go, because he did finally credit my card, but it really made me angry to be told that the delay was because they were busy doing their jobs-I am a customer, so dealing with my concerns is their job. I still have no idea what happened. I still don't understand why they said they didn't have the wheelchair when they did. Who used it??I made certain choices for my vacation with the idea in mind of having a beach wheelchair. In Rincon, we stayed at an inn on the ocean with a beautiful swimming pool. We could have stayed someplace less expensive, but we wanted to be by the water. The particular beach wheelchair I rented allows for access to the beach AND to swimming pools. So I was expecting to be able to swim every day. Instead, I was able to swim in the ocean only once, the day we visited the Mar sin Barreras facility at Boqueron (they have beach wheelchairs there for disabled visitors). The entire time I was in Puerto Rico, I was able to look at the ocean, but I was not able to go for walks on the beach with my brother, I was not able to swim in the ocean more than once, I was not able to swim in the pool. It was kind of like going to the mountains for a ski trip, and the hotel gives your skis to someone else, and there isn't a single pair available for rental. So you're in ski heaven, but YOU can't ski, you can only bundle up, enjoy the weather and watch everybody else. Thanks, Hotel El Convento. If you had answered my email, explained what happened, and refunded me promptly, I would have given you credit for caring about your customers--mistakes happen. As it is, I think you were trying to take advantage of me. I don't believe you had any intention of answering my email, and if I hadn't persisted, you would never have responded.

<Content>Fabulous 24 hours! We had a bad experience elsewhere in the City, called El Convento after a sleepless night. Could they book us a room for tonight? Could we check in early? We were in Puerto RIco only to go to VIeques and just by chance had to spend two nights in San Juan before heading back up north. We now would return to San Juan just to spend time in El Convento. This place is wonderful and worth the price!

<Author>iwannalilsunshine
<Content>Great location, less than great customer service We spent 2 nights at this hotel over the Easter holiday. Check-in was a lengthy process since the front desk manager gave us a smaller room than the one we booked and attempted to convince us that we were incorrect despite our having paperwork documenting our specific reservation. This problem was resolved after a few hours and we did receive a room consistent with our booking. The room was fairly small however and one of the showers leaked due to poor grading of the tile. We did report this to the front desk. We heard many customer service complaints while we were there. We were given conflicting and inaccurate information about an excursion to El Yunque. On a positive note, Shannon at the front desk was professional and helpful. The hotel itself is quite pretty and in an excellent location. You can easily walk to the forts and around Old San Juan. Breakfast at the hotel was excellent and service was good. The wine and cheese hour was good, with a wide selection of wines and cheeses. The hotel was clean with comfortable common areas and many antiques. Overall, after check in, our experience was very positive mainly due to the hotel's location. El Yunque is worth the trip if you can plan a day to visit. The pool is postage stamp sized but the view from the pool area is amazing.

<Author>theLAgirls
<Content>Expensive but best in Old San Juan The hotel is really beautiful and perfectly situated in Old San Juan. There aren't many hotel options so if you can afford it, we'd definitely recommend El Convento. We stayed in two rooms (see below) and both were unique, comfortable, clean and beautiful. Unfortunately we were in OSJ for such a short time that we didn't enjoy many of the amenities of the hotel - wine hour, pool, restaurants - which we regret especially for the price.Our one issue --Due to flight delays, we missed the entire first night of our two night stay at El Convento. While paying about $350/night, this was a huge bummer. We had called ahead to say we would be very late, but when we checked in the following morning, our requested bed arrangement had been given away and all they had was one queen bed. Since we had paid for the night, we felt cheated. They kept saying that they had to give it away since we weren't there but our opinion was that we paid for it so it should have been there. After our reserved room became available later that day, they moved us. When we complained to a manager upon check out, she did give us 15% of the first night but was fairly rude about it and clearly told us we were at fault for not arriving earlier. We realize we reserved it so we should pay, but the attitude left a bad taste in our mouths. All in all - we weren't overwhelmed with the attentiveness of the staff. Our baggage had been delayed and delivered to the hotel later in the day. When we arrived back at our room, there appeared to be a message on the phone. But the voicemail didn't work so I called to the front desk for my message, which was never delivered to us. Come to find out, the message said our baggage was downstairs, and had been for hours, and we had been making do with the same travelling clothes for two days. Also, it was very crowded/Easter weekend and many people were at the front desk with complaints, of varying sorts, so we weren't the only ones with issues.

<Content>Old World elegance We spent three days at El Convento before debarking on a cruise and those three days were wonderful, ammenities are above most exclusive hotels. Our problem arose on our return from the cruise. We had reservations for one night before flying home. We wanted to relax after the cruise and not rush to the airport. Upon arrival they told us we could not have a room until 3:00 p.m. Having not slept well the night before I was exhausted and wanted to just lay down. Waiting 3 hours in a very uncomfortable lobby and another 3 hours up on the 3rd floor in their honor bar area was exhausting. Next time we stay in San Juan I think we will pick one of the bigger hotels where we know we can get into a room upon arrival. This small boutique hotel is just not equipped with enough staff. Having check out at 11 a.m. I can't understand why it would take 6 hours to clean so few rooms unless they don't have enough help. Try the El San Juan Hotel and Casino across from the airport. Wow, they've done an amazing job with this hotel.

<Author>congogal
<Content>Definitely would want to return...... El Convento is one of the most amazing places to stay in Old San Juan. It is the ideal base to explore the Old city. It has the most beautiful atmosphere and the grounds were outstanding. It is within walking distance of everything such as restaurants, interesting tourist sites, and the waterfront area. They have gorgeous historic reminders of the convent as it once was, and it really made you wonder what it was like to have been there in the day. The staff was very friendly, the service exceptional, we felt like family in this homey small hotel. Each evening we enjoyed a complimentary wine  cheese reception by the library, with quality wines that were delicious and well chose, as well as internet access so we could do two things at once. The restaurants in the hotel were excellent, we tried two out of the four due to limited time restraints. We definitely recommend El Patio del Nispero and lunch at C茫na, both were unsurpassed. Room service was also quick and efficient. We spent alot of time reading  relaxing on the incredible roofdeck, which boasted amazing views and a small pool for cooling off.Our room had a partial view of San Juan Bay, which made the room so enjoyable, and the luxurious sheets, towels  toiletries lived up to our high standards. The bed was abviously of the highest quality and the flat screen TV was a luxury we don't get to enjoy at all hotels. If only we had planned more for our trip, we would have gladly stayed there longer, but we would definitely stay there again in the future. Thank you.

<Author>lolamini
<Content>Great hotel in a lovely area I recently stayed for one night at El Convento in Old San Juan. It is a lovely hotel set in a building with a long and interesting history. The lobby area feels like you stepped into a museum or an important building of some kind and it's decorated in old pieces to bring out the historic nature of the structure. I had read other reviews that the staff was not responsive to guests, but we had the opposite experience. Our room wasn't ready when we arrived, so the front desk, which was very helpful, stored our bags, told us how to get an internet connection up in their library (which is a nice area with coffee/drinks etc), and then they came up shortly after to tell us our room was ready. There is a pretty bar/lounge in the courtyard of the hotel with a giant tree going all the way up in the middle of the courtyard.The pool, on the roof top, is quite small, with a hot tub next to it, but there are lounge chairs and it's nice to sit and look out at the old city. Our room had a huge and well-stocked bathroom and was decorated in a unique manner;definitely not the usual chain hotel room. The only negative in the room was that it had a queen size bed (they didn't have many rooms with Kings) which moved when you leaned back against the bedboard to watch TV. The hotel is located in an utterly charming part of San Juan - small hilly cobblestone streets, with pretty buildings, cafes, stores etc., and it's also just a few blocks from the forts and the water. I would definitely stay here again.

We enjoyed our stay tremendously, the staff was always friendly, helpful and courteous and we would recommend the hotel highly to anyone staying in lovely Old San Juan.

<Content>NIce stay in Old Town from a frequent traveler We stayed at the El Covento to experience the charm of Old San Juan (this hotel is not the place to stay if you want to relax by the pool or beach). However it is a lovely place to stay if you want to shop, eat and experience some history. A good place for couples. A great place for adults- I would not recommend bringing children. It was quiet and beautiful albeit somewhat expensive (an additional $90 in fees PER night for hotel tariff/taxes in addtition to the nightly hotel rate when booking trhu the hotel website). Walking distance to many great restaurants, and the forts. There is a small but very nice hot tub on the roof with a beautiful view. The pool is TINY. You do have the ability to use one of the beaches in Isla Verde. There is a complimentary wine and cheese reception every evening which was very nice. If checking out at noon- i may recommend checking out a little early because there is somewhat of a crowd. My husband and I stayed here for a few days to experience the city and the restaurants and then moved to a beach resort to enjoy some surf and sun... (which is what i recommend doing if coming to san juan for the first time)Cons of the hotel: 1. Small pool2. I thought our tariff was slightly expensive (a little over 800$ for 2 nights) 3. Frazzled staff when checking out on Monday afternoon- come earlier than noon if you want to beat the line (however, staff was normally polite and helpful during the other parts of the stay)Restaurants in walking distance:-Marmalade- great food, atmosphere ($30 per entree)-DragonFly- small restaurant, but great food, service is only OK/ sometimes rude on the weekends when it is exptremely busy at prime hours- but food makes up for it. may have long wait. <Author>kad213
<Content>Didn't want to leave... This was my first venture to Puerto Rico and I was doing a solo trip...just really needed a break from everything. I followed the advice of many on TripAdvisor and decided to take a chance with El Convento - I am very glad I did! The hotel staff were VERY nice and knowledgeable of the area and things to do. I have never stayed at a historical European-style hotel before (I am used to the big chains, such as Ritz, Marriott, etc.) but I quickly became very fond of the hotel's historical charm and beauty. The hotel is located in the heart of Old San Juan and is walking distance from hundreds of shops, restaurants, bars, clubs, museums, and other historically significant sites. It was great to leisurely walk the streets of Old San Juan. As a single traveler, I felt very safe in the hotel, as you need a key to access all levels except the main floor. The views from the deck are phenomenal, and the daily wine  cheese reception was very refreshing while providing an opportunity to mingle with other travelers. During my stay, there was a 10k I was considering running, but registration had closed. I mentioned this to the front desk staff while having a general conversation about things to do in the area and for the next two days they did everything possible to try to get me in the race - unfortunately, they were not able to, but it was the simple fact that a brief conversation led them to go through so much effort on my behalf - which revealed to me what a special hotel this was!!!!The next time I go to Puerto Rico, I will be at the Hotel El Convento.

<Author>BeverlyGuy
<Content>Charming Hotel, Enhanced by Superior Service by Staff We selected El Convento, with no prior knowledge of Puerto Rico or the hotel, using Trip Advisor...and we were very well advised indeed. The hotel is not a beach resort. It is wonderfully located in the most historic part of Old San Juan. The location across from the cathedral and very near to the primary shopping areas allows for walking nearly everywhere in the old city--the museums, restaurants, historic buildings and waterfront. There is a free shuttle bus loop should you tire of walking, or want to begin your day at the far end of town.The hotel is an historic building begun in the 17th century, and was one of the early historic preservation efforts in the old town when it was converted from commercial use to hotel in the 1960s by a member of the Woolworth family. Today it has just over 50 rooms, plus a lovely terrace and plunge pool on the roof with harbor and town views, a nice gathering area where wine and cheese are generously served each evening, restaurants and meeting facilities. Our room was not large, but we had access to so many other facilities--including nice tables in the open air hallways of the hotel--that it did not much matter. The bathroom was also quite small, as is often the case with historic hotels. If you are looking for space, this is not the place for you. The furniture was dated, but the room was clean and had doors that opened to a harbor view. There was an up-to-date flat screen TV and complimentary hard-wire internet access (as well as a computer in the library for those not traveling with their own). Linens were clean, and towels were promptly replaced during turn down service. Air conditioning was just adequate, and would definitely be a concern in warmer months. The hotel building and furnishings are comfortable, not lavish, but the staff is exceptional. The evening wine reception was truly a chance to meet and interact with staff and other guests, not the usual one glass of cheap wine and run. We enjoyed our fellow travelers and talking with staff, and we got lots of pointers on restaurants and things to do. Judith, the front desk manager who is originally from Sweden but has 17 years in Puerto Rico, was particularly welcoming as well as wonderfully efficient. She and the entire staff team never failed to be welcoming, courteous and helpful. That put the real luxury into the stay.There is access to a beach club at Isla Verde, which is actually the Marriott Courtyard Hotel, adjacent to the airport. This requires a $20+tip taxi ride each way, but once there we were treated very well and the beach was superb. You can sign for food expenses at the Marriott that are billed back to your El Convento account, so you need not carry much money or credit cards for your time on the beach.We dined twice at the in-house Tapas restaurant, a nice follow-up to the healthy serving of cheeses at the wine reception. Breakfast in the courtyard was very good with good service, but the morning kitchen is very slow. Our 5 night stay was at rack rate in high season, so it was not inexpensive. The hotel is used by cruise lines for pre-departure stays, and some travelers reported much-discounted room rates...but only for one night. We felt that we received good value due to location, historic ambience and the very special treatment given by all of the staff. If you want a beach resort, or the most up to date interior design, El Convento is not for you. If you want to be in Old San Juan with easy access to cultural sites and wonderful dining, and with an atmosphere that reflects a very historic place very well, then select El Convento. We are very glad that we did.  
<Date>Feb 14, 2008

<Author>genwebb
<Content>Charming and Beautiful, only a few issues We went to San Juan for a wedding last May and stayed at El Convento, which was also the location of the wedding. My initial impression, admittedly, was not that great. Our rooms were not ready when we arrived an hour early - no big deal. After all, we were early. But they were aware that we were there and when we came back at check-in the rooms were still not ready. It took about an hour of waiting in the lobby for them to prepare our rooms for us. This was NOT just me and my fiance; it was multiple other groups (probably 5 or 6 groups total). It was incredibly hot that day, and while we sat there sweating bullets we were not even offered a glass of water or anything else for our inconvenience.The only reason that I did not formally complain about this was because the experience was all uphill from there. We were shown to our room which we found to be kind of oldish, but very charming with a giant fluffy bed and reasonable accomodations. Also, every room has a very nice flat screen tv, which I thought was very cool. The AC in our room wasn't that great and the housekeeping staff kept turning it off which was annoying because it took SO long to cool the room down.The actual hotel though, and the giant courtyard and the fantastic views from the roof really did make a pleasant experience all around for us. The pool was stunningly small... it is just a miniature thing to put your legs in, and I thought the water smelled funny. The hot tub on the roof was great, I thought it seemed pretty clean, and the view from it overlooking the water is awesome!The groundskeeping is great, the place is well kept and again the courtyard is stunning. The food is pretty decent but a tad overpriced for what you get. I am pretty picky - I thought all of the food in San Juan was overpriced for the quality.You can sort of hear everything through the doors because of the way the hotel is set up - they have 2 doors to your room to combat this, so no big deal. Mosquitos are after me no matter where I go, this was no different, so bring your mosquito spray when you go to San Juan.All in all we really had a great time here and the wedding we attended was WONDERFUL. My friend said their wedding staff was very accomodating as well. I would stay here again in the future and I would recommend this hotel to others!

<Author>barbara_2000
<Content>Great Hotel, Good Location with some minor problems. Hotel El Convento is located on the corner of the very narrow, busy, noisy streets of San Juan. We arrived early from our cruise ship and were greeted by Fernando, who made us feel welcomed immediately. He took care of our luggage and stored it until we came back later when our room was ready. The desk clerks were very helpful and suggested we walk around and have some lunch and check back about 1 p.m. to see if our room was ready. We walked down the hill from the hotel and found plenty of shopping. A Coach store, Dooney and Bourke store, Polo store, and a Guess store were just a few of the shopping options within three blocks of the hotel. Just past the Dooney and Bourke store is a great place to have an afternoon frozen drink and a taco. It is called Maria's and they serve the best drinks in San Juan. Up the street from the hotel (towards El Morro) is a great place to grab a hamburger called El Patio De Sam. Fort El Morro is within walking distance and we took the free shuttle service to other Fort.Upon returning to the hotel at 1 p.m. our room was still not ready so we waited in the beautiful courtyard of the hotel. They have bar service there so you can get a refreshing drink while you wait.Our room was ready at 3 p.m. and we were given Room 103 which was a little hard to find since there are only three rooms on the first floor and it has an entrance around the corner from the elevator. The room was large with two queen beds, a full bath and separate room with a shower. The mattress left a lot to be desired. Upon sitting down, every spring in the mattress could be felt. Needless to say I spent two sleepless nights in San Juan. Another problem was the toilet. Usually a toilet seat covers the toilet bowl. This toilet seat was about an inch smaller than the bowl and moved all over the place.On our second day in San Juan we came back from a tour to find the room next door had put their lunch trays in the hall on a table. When we departed 24 hours later, they were still there. The food was starting to smell. When we checked out, I mentioned all of the above to the lady at the front desk and she apologized and said she would have someone check on it.All in all the hotel is very nice and located in a great area for sightseeing and shopping. I am not sure I would stay there again due to the three problems I listed above.  
<Date>Jan 16, 2008

<Author>deafbat
<Content>Terrible service - don't stay here! My friend and I decided to stay at this hotel after reading a review of it in the New York Times. Unfortunately, our stay there turned out to be a horrible experience.On our first day at the hotel, we asked the front desk to book us a tour for the following evening. We were assured that it would be taken care of. The next morning, we dropped by the front desk to check on the status of the tour, and were told that while it had not yet been booked, it would be done and we were to report to the lobby that evening for the tour. We came by in the evening as told, and found out that the tour had never been booked!We were angry and disappointed at having our plans fall through, but decided to give it another try. We asked the front desk to book us a tour for the next day. This time, the tour was indeed booked, but the front desk quoted us the wrong price - repeatedly. We were told that the cost was $110 for the two of us - we even checked twice to make sure that this was correct - but in the end, the tour guide told us that the cost of the tour was $110 per person. We felt disgusted and let down by the incompetence of the hotel's front desk.In addition, when we went down to the front desk to make known our bad experiences, we encountered another couple whom the hotel had lost the luggage of, forgetting which room it had been brought to. They had to do a room-by-room search to locate the luggage. Yet another two people we encountered had been allocated a room that, it seemed, had already been allocated to someone else. Such incompetence is terribly unseemly of a hotel that has had so many positive reviews in various places.The final insult was when we asked to see a manager to make our concerns known, the manager in question treated us with the utmost disrespect, brushing off our comments and not taking us seriously. Her only response to us was, so do you want me to book you into another hotel?In conclusion, our experience at the Hotel El Convento was a complete nightmare, and I am writing this review to warn fellow travelers about the terrible service there in the hopes that they will not have the same awful experience that my friend and I did.

<Author>SAMAID
<Content>Still Beautiful, traditional and Unique But in Need of Repairs Just finished a late Dec. stay at the El Convento and it is still beautiful (stayed there before). Interior Courtyard is truly gorgeous and such a restful place to sit and have coffee. However, the rooms and hotel common areas are certainly in need of repair. The hotel hot tub has a thick layer of mold around the top and is completly cracked and broken. The wall above the pool is also cracked and in need of paint. While our room had a lovely balcony and was the standard unique el convento style -- our sheets had holes in them and the tub was stain and cracked and in need of repair.In addition, the staff is very friendly but quite inadept with directions and recommendations. Three times we got wrong directions/addresses (for locations as close as three blocks away), reservations were made but we were never informed (they forgot) and information on major attractions such as the Bio Bay and the Bacardi Distillery were faulty if they had any information at all.That said, the location is the best in town, much rather stay in Old San Juan for the food and entertainment and walking proximity to the fort and piers etc. There is a great flamenco restaurant across the little square outside the hotel and La Bombombera can't be beat for any meal especially breakfast.We paid less than $200 to stay and that made it worth is but as the price of El Convento creeps up they must really make more of an effort to ensure the little things are kept up as well (holes in sheets are just unacceptable)

<Content>Elegant Hotel with Very Small Dark Rooms We stayed at El Convento for two nights. The public areas of the hotel are elegant, and the staff friendly and helpful - although not well-trained or efficient. When we inquired about the message light on our phone going on the second morning that we were there, and us not being able to access the message (we were expecting a call from our son who was arriving later that day at the hotel), the day staff at the hotel was not at all quick to try solving the problem and took several hours trying to figure out the code to access the message (it should have been the arrival date, but wasn't) and finally determined that the message was an old message. They couldn't even figure out how to turn off the message light, so it kept on blinking. Finally, in the evening, the desk clerk knew exactly what to do, and fixed the problem in a few seconds.The first room that we were taken to was fairly large, but the air conditioner was obviously being worked on (part of the ceiling insulation was on the floor), and the bellhop immediately called the desk to assign us another room. That room was very small and dark - and not exceptionally clean. The time was getting close to midnight, and after a delayed flight and a time change of four hours, we just wanted to get to sleep.The wine and cheese hour was very nice with a nice selection of wines and cheeses.We love Old San Juan, and El Convento is in a very convenient location. We were able to walk to San Cristobal Fort and took the free trolley to El Morro Fort. The hotel is close to the only remaining city gate. It is also close to lots of shopping.Go to La Bombonera for breakfast (259 Calle San Francisco), and be sure to order a Mallorca. It's about a five minute walk from the hotel.
