<Content>Enchanting El Convento This was a marvelous way to celebrate my husbands 59th birthday. The month of October is perfect without the holiday crowds. It was our first time in Puerto Rico. <Author>WrestlingEuphony
<Content>Non-Weekends are 100% better We stayed at this hotel for 4 nights prior to our cruise (Sunday departure).The hotel was everything we expected it to be: unique, charming, old world, etc. with all the amenities you would expect: robes, turn-down service, fabulous concierge, etc.We asked for (and got) a room on a high floor (5th i think?) with a view of the bay. It is WELL worth the extra money. Looking out over the rooftops and the water is amazing. And because the climate is so prone to short rainstorms, it's quite a site to watch the clouds roll in and the lightning start!Breakfast in the garden patio every morning was beautiful, with perfect service and delcious food (it's costly, but there's no where else to get breakfast in San Juan practically).The tapas hour every night on the promenade was our highlight. Delicious cheeses and wines and a nice seat outdoors - it was heaven.We used the concierge to book a trip to El Yunque for us and to call taxis a few times - it was a great service. Everything about this hotel was romantic and classy and wonderful....except - when the other cruisers checked in.On Friday (and worse on Saturday) - a total barrage of Cruisers took over the hotel. The fact that it was crowded was unpleasant, but more than that (and i'm about to sound snobby) was that so many of the cruisers seemed out of place at El Convento - they were loud, they were dressed inappropriately, they had throngs of screaming children, etc.When you're shelling out this much money to stay at a luxury hotel, you don't expect it to turn into a holiday inn overnight.For example: El convento has an honor bar - where they leave out bottles of booze, mixers, soda, snacks, etc with a little sign that says this is an honor bar, if you make something for yourself, please fill out a receipt and leave it in this box - your room will be charged - on Wednesday and Thursday night the honor bar was honored - on Friday and Saturday my husband and I watched as handfulls of new guests (cruisers) stole from the bar - many of them laughing about it while they were doing it. some of them going so far as to grab armfulls of bottled soda and water and carry it back to their room!That was the only downside of El Convento, some of the losers it brought in they day before the cruise.  
<Date>Oct 9, 2007

<Author>kimcorbettrn
<Content>Beautiful, unique "hotel" and very romantic What a great find!! This hotel is not your typical hotel. We had a wonderful stay, from the time my husband and I arrived via taxi from the airport the bellman, Luis was there to assist us, with our luggage and a smile. After check in, Luis, showed us to our room and showed us where everything was, including the ice machines, pool and hot tub, wine reception venue each evening and told us about each of the resturants within the hotel. The room was very comfortable, cozy and clean, and decorated beautifully. Each room has flat screen TV and Bose radios. The hotel has a nice wine and cheese reception each evening on the patio which is very nice to sit out on and relax , and the view is exceptional, it overlooks the San Juan Bay. The pool is small but very nice and serves its purpose and you could not ask for a better panoramic view of San Juan.There are plenty of lounge chairs and sitting room in the pool/hot tub area. I can not say enough good things about El Convento, its not your typical hotel but is a very nice and unique place to stay. My husband and I stayed here for 4 nights for our honeymoon and they had a beautiful flower arrangement, champagne, and chocolates waiting in our room when we arrived from dinner our first night. The hotel is in a great location, close to pier, in Old San Juan and shopping, great resturants, the forts all within walking distance, the hotel will even assist you in arranging tours to El Yunque Rain forest, the Phosphorescent bays, etc. Venus and Carlos, in reservations, were very helpful in assisting me with my reservations. You will not be disappointed. We will definitally come back here to stay again.

<Author>favre96
<Content>Excellent hotel, great location My wfie and I stayed here over Labor Day weekend and can't say enough good things about this hotel.1. If you have the opportunity, book a Deluxe room. These rooms are located on floors 4  5. Our room overlooked the bay which was cool to see the storms/cargo ships pass through. The room itself was elegantly decorated. The huge flat screen TV and Bose sound system were major pluses. 2. Another tip is to book via the hotels website. I did a ton of research and you can't beat the price from [--].3. The hotel has three restaurants. Each restaurant has a good selection of authentic dishes. We recommend eating at all three.4. Located in old San Juan. Within a few blocks from the water. There are wonderful restaurants and tons of places to shop (Coach, Puma, etc) all around the hotel.5. The staff is attentive and courteous. The shower head was spraying water every where and within 10 minutes someone was up fixing the problem.6. The hotel recommended the Eden Spa. My wife had a miserable experience. She said that it would have been worth the cab fare to go the spa at the Ritz or another well known resort.7. The only thing I would hope the hotel would add at some point is room service for lunch and dinner.

<Author>crackofdawn
<Content>Another "5" No Surprise We've frequently visited Old San Juan, but last week's trip was our first opportunity to stay at El Convento. I'd certainly agree with the other top reviews. We stayed 2 nights and thoroughly enjoyed the all smiles on deck attitude of every staff member you meet in the hotel. I know they must have some bad days, but you'd never know. TIP: don't bother trying to drive into/park in Old San Juan-- even the taxis have problems negotiating the streets. A cab for 2 people with 4 suitcases from the airport, with tip is about $26-27.Over the months prior from booking to actual staying, I watched the hotel's website for changes to their rates and was pleased to find rates in the $160 range shortly before we left. Do watch their website for similar changes and packages.I also enjoyed the LG lcd 37 television in the room and the BOSE Wave radio. Bring your MP3 player and connecting cable!Couple of good restaurants within walking distance that we've enjoyed in the past and this last trip: Amadeus Cafe and La Mallorquina. We tried a couple of newer ones (for us). We tried Raices on Recinto Sur (behind the Sheraton) -- very noisy and not impressed with the food. And the other, for lunch, I don't have the name but it is two doors west of Amadeus -- very attractive decor with good rates and I noticed several menu items geared for kids, as well.

<Author>ddmg730
<Content>disappointed with El Convento My family and I (2 children) stayed at the El Convento post cruise. We arrived at the hotel at about noon. We were dropped off at valet parking, and had to carry our bags across the street and into the hotel. Check in was at 4:00 and they held our bags for us until our room was ready. It wasn't ready until 4:20 . It seemed like forever with 2 kids after an exhausting trip. Our room was wonderful, however they lost 2 of our bags. One was found and brought up to our room, but the other remains a mystery. It contained our prescription medications, 3 pairs of shoes, and several articles of clothing. We frequently checked back with the front desk who assured us they would find it, but everytime we checked back they didn't know anything about it and would try and give us some one else's bag that was in their store room.We had an early flight the next morning and still no sign of our luggage bag. We completed the guest questionaire which supposedly goes directly to the manager, but still have not heard anything from the hotel in a month. Very dissapointing. Also, the hotel charged our credit card an additional $12.00 10 days after we checked out with no explanation. My husband called once more and was told it was a municipality tax, but we were never told about it at check in or check out. We booked the room via hotwire and were asssured that all taxes were allready paid.They seem to have poor follow through to resolve any conflicts.Certainly not what we would expect from a luxury hotel.

<Author>selecthotels
<Content>An Absolute Treasure!! This hotel gets 5 stars from me. You can read all the other reviews to get a fuller picture and also look at their website but I would like to extole their virtues in a somewhat different manner.Service, service, service and always with a smile. From arrival to departure we had 5 days and nights of sheer enjoyment.Front desk, always manned, alert and attentive. Directions and recommendations for restaurants, churches, museum's, etc professionally given. Valets and Porters(who all speak English) quick and attentive and on more than one occasion in the elevators they mentioned that we shouldn't miss the free cheese and wine being held each evening from 6-7pm, which was superb by the way.Rooms, spotlessly clean, authentically Spanish in design(as is the whole Hotel). Maid service, prompt, smiling, efficient and turndown service was also included and found this to be more superior than many other top-rated hotels we have stayed at.Room service was answered quickly and delivered quickly and again, always with a smile. What the hotel website doesn't make abundantly clear is that outside each one of the rooms, you have your own table and chairs, where you can drink, eat and smoke(if you wish)whilst enjoying the fabulous views of their 300 year old nispero fruit tree from Spain and all the other plants, whilst refreshing breezes and great music wafts the senses.On the third floor one finds complimentary tea, coffee, iced water and assorted nuts(24 hours) plus an extensive honour bar and a Library that houses free internet services.As mentioned before, you can read all of this in other reviews..what I want to bring to the traveller who has not visited San Juan or indeed the El Convento is a Hotel that clearly strives to stand out from all the rest and actually achieves this difficult task by offering the kind of atmosphere and service, be it in any of their many outstanding Restaurants or from difficult to simple requests, that sometimes get that scorned Caribbean frowned upon look elsewhere in this part of the world. We have all been there, havent we?I have actually seen Management walk around and talk to the guests, asking how their stay is or was and can they do anything more for them? So if one is able to find a hotel that is fanatical about making sure their guests come first, no matter what and always trying to improve(as nothing runs like clockwork), plus have possibly the best position in all of downtown San Juan, followed by stunning hotel scenery and authentic culture, well one just hopes that one can return in the near future. I know I will.Finally, if you are the sort of person who relishes glitz, gambling, noise and hob-nobbing with people, especially around the usual brash pool, go elsewhere. If you require authentic refined elegance and beauty from another era, backed up with truly outstanding service, you have possibly found a hidden secret and from my point of view one of the most exclusive hotels in the Caribbean.

<Author>marisol-7
<Content>The Best Visit Ever We just had our best trip ever to the Hotel El Convento in Old San Juan. This was our fifth stay at this hotel and we are very happy we chose to return. It is a small boutique hotel. The entire staff went out of their way to make us feel like family. Our room was very comfortable with a great view of San Juan Harbor. It included a flat screen TV, Bose radio, and there is nightly turndown service.The architecture of the hotel is very beautiful and soothing after a day of sightseeing. The walls of this former convent must be very thick because we never heard a sound at night, and I am a light sleeper. Even though it is a small hotel there are some nice amenities. It has three restaurants. The tapas one Il Picoteo has excellent tapas. The rooftop pool is a relaxing place to cool down in the late afternoon.There is a complimentary wine reception in the evening fron 6:00-7:00. It offers a very nice selection of wines in addition to fruit and cheese. It is a great way to meet other guests and hear about their experiences.Feliciano the doorman has been there since we started staying there. He is one of the nicest people you will ever meet. He can also answer any of your questions about Old San Juan.We are already looking forward to planning our next trip to the Hotel El Convento.

<Author>sweetsie
<Content>Gorgeous Hotel, Convenient Location The El Convento is a beautiful old hotel. The rooms are rustic (it's an old building!), but very charming. The courtyard is gorgeous with beautiful palms, plants and flowers. There are all kinds of nooks andniches to check out in the hotel--patios, restaurants, bars, a library! The staff was very friendly and helpful and our room was kept very clean for the entire stay.The location is great for exploring Old San Juan on foot. There are many bars, restaurants and shops in the area. If you don't absolutelyneed a car, don't get one! Driving in Old San Juan is a nightmare. The streets are just too narrow, and parking is practically impossible. However the hotel does have a valet parking service available. We'll definitely go back again.

<Author>hardychica
<Content>Old World style, boutique hotel details We stayed at the El Convento for 2 nights and really admired the charm and architecture of the building. The hotel is in an old convent and retains much of its Spanish style architecture. Our room was clean with details that made you feel like you weren't in your typical, everyday room. From the art on the wall (black and white photographs), to the alarm clock/CD player (Bose), and the brand new flat screen TVs the hotel went that extra step to justify the expensive price. The hotel also hosted a daily wine  cheese bar from 6-7 for all hotel guests free of charge. There was also a full bar based on the honor system for those who wanted more than just wine to drink. It was so nice to finish a day of traveling around Old San Juan with a glass of wine, watching the sun set on the terrace. Speaking of the terrace, the pool is very tiny and is more like a dipping pool. We didn't mind because when we're in cities, we get out and explore. That said, it was still very nice to cool off after a hot day exploring the city. Other than that, the staff was extremely courteous and helpful. Our rooms were always cleaned and the location was fantastic. We were able to walk everywhere we needed to go. The only reason I didn't get ive it 5 stars is because it is expensive. I don't stay in a lot of hotels in this price range so I can't compare it with other hotels at this price, but I think that accomodations in Puerto Rico tend to be pretty expensive in general. I did move on to the Westin Rio Mar after staying here and while the grounds of that hotel were nice, I still think it was lacking some of the charming extras that I received at El Convento.

<Author>pfg07
<Content>Totally torn I, like others on this website, am torn about my time spent at El Convento.The hotel itself is majestic. Located in the heart of Old San Juan, my wife and I were able to walk to all of our desired sights. We enjoyed the complementary wine and cheese reception every evening and also enjoyed the plunge pool on the roof of the hotel. The rooms were like history themselves with modern updates - vaulted ceilings, Spanish marble floors juxtaposed with a Bose CD player and flat screen TV.That being said, my wife and I paid over $400 (US) to stay at the hotel. When we first arrived, our bathroom did not appear to be cleaned (urine stains on the toilet seat) and it took three phone calls to get someone to clean it. Additionally, we rented a car while in San Juan - somehow a light was left on in the car (we think by the valet as he was in the car last although we are not sure) and were not apologized to for this inconvenience nor were we helped by the hotel staff.Overall, our stay was nice (this is a very nice hotel, please do not get me wrong) although for the money we spent we expected so much more.

<Author>Stineman
<Content>A feast fo the senses. On a recent trip to Puerto Rico my wife and I had the opportunity to leave the kids with family and get away for a little time by ourselves. After receiving recommendations from family and friends we decided to stay at the El Convento Hotel.We were not disappointed!The beauty and grandeur of the hotel with it's high ceilings, arched doorways and marble floors impacted us as soon as we walked through the front doors. The walkways between the rooms and the courtyard were wide and airy. The courtyard with the nispero tree and tropical plants is tranquil and welcoming. The rooms are comfortable and well appointed -- they even have electricity and running water (a thing unheard of in buildings built over 300 years ago:-) . The restaurants are great; we particularly enjoyed a relaxing late night visit with friends at El Picoteo over Cafe-con-leche, Tres Leches cake and Creme Brulee. However, if you prefer to find a place off property ther are many options to choose from and all within walking distance from the hotel.We found the staff to be attentive, helpful and friendly, a combination not often found in hotels of the caliber of El Convento.Located in historic Old San Juan, sharing the old city's charm and allure while adding to it a blend of old and new to create an atmosphere that is both unique and captivating, my wife put it best when she described El Convento Hotel as a feast for the senses.

<Author>sfmartinez
<Content>We could not have been happier with our stay here! I cannot say enough good things about this hotel. I went with my husband and our very active toddler in December, and we had a wonderful stay here. The hotel is incredibly charming and elegant, and located in the heart of Old San Juan. We had rented a car, but ended up leaving it in their parking lot for our entire stay because we could walk everywhere. It is also across the street from the Children's museum, which was a nice place to go to give our little one a break. Our room was large, super clean, with very high ceilings. And the staff was terrific. The one criticism I had was that the on-site restaurants were very expensive, but I guess you'd expect that at such a nice hotel. There are a lot of cheaper places to eat nearby. One tip- call the hotel directly for their rates. We had searched online for deals for this hotel and were convinced it was out of our price range, but my husband called the hotel directly, said we would be in town to visit family, and was quoted a rate more than $100 less per day than the cheapest price we had seen on the internet. We will go back to this place every time we visit Puerto Rico.

<Author>Dr_owheatl
<Content>Outstanding service in the most beautiful of cities I would like to preface this comment by stating that I travel extensively for business and for leisure. When I book my travel, I always aim for safety, cleanliness, and accessibility. If I am lucky, good service will come along with the other criteria. At El Convento, I found everything except good service. Instead, I found OUTSTANDING SERVICE.There are very few places for which I will actually take the time to sit down and write a review, in fact, this is the second attempt since the first review did not upload. But because I feel so strongly about my wonderful experiences at El Convento, I am determined to get my review posted.I have always been treated like royalty at this hotel but never more so than the time when I required extensive assistance due to travelling while recovering from surgery to repair a broken ankle. I could not have travelled had I not been coming to El Convento to stay.I was helped in every imaginable manner by ALL of the hotel staff. A shower chair was placed in my room, a chair with wheels was immediately sent to my room so I could manage better in the room (I did not want a wheelchair) extra pillows to elevate the leg at night were always brought in, extra blankets, ice for my ice bag, as well as extra water and coffee. Oh, and they scanned the room to anticipate possible problems for me and then determined that they would remove all the area rugs and move the furniture to insure my safety.During the nightly wine reception, the managers would place an extra chair for my leg, sit me down and would proceed to bring me my favorite wine, a plate with a generous serving from their extensive selection of cheese and crackers, and a bundle of grapes to top the plate.As I progressed from being in a boot with two crutches to being able to walk unassisted (a period of over four months) they celebrated with me and applauded me as I would show off my steps. They all went above and beyond the call of duty. Truly, if you are looking for a place with top notch service, nestled in the most beautiful of cities, there is no better place to go to than the El Convento Hotel in Old San Juan.

<Author>zjtravel
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location We stayed in the El Convento in March during a weekday. We had a wonderful experience. Both my husband and I have traveled extensively and I would say this is definitely one of the best small hotels we've been too. We booked two rooms(one for us and one for my parents) at a special mid week price at $230 per night(a steal for Old San Juan). They reserve you a room but don't assign you a specific room until you arrive. As soon as we stepped onto the hotel property someone met us and took our luggage. When we checked in, they had my parent's room ready but ours wasn't. As an apology, they gave my parents a suite next to the pool and assured us that our room would be ready within the hour. True to their word our room was ready in less than an hour and they gave us a top floor suite with our own private deck overlooking Old San Juan as a thank you for our patience. The hotel offers a wine tasting from 6-7pm every night with great wine choices and a fabulous selection of gourmet cheeses and crackers. The location is excellent--within walking distance of all the historic sights. The rooms are tastefully decorated with relatively new furniture keeping with the convent's history and spanish theme. As for complaints about being interrupted in the early evening by housekeeping--it was for the hotel's early evening turn down service. They do it during the wine tasting hours as a little extra. My husband and I would stay here again and again. The staff was helpful and the rooms clean and the location the best in Old San Juan.

<Content>Felt like a convent I stayed at El Convento last week for two nights on my way to Antigua. We planned on staying an additional third night before returning to the US until we experienced what felt like being trapped in a convent. The two nights were awful. The hotel is way overprized for what you get. The rooms are mediocre at best. We stayed in two different rooms and in both rooms the flat screen TV buzzed. The bathroom in the second room was missing a bath stopper and had no water pressure. When we were napping someone attempted to enter the room in the early evening (not during cleaning hours). We asked the front desk and they knew nothing of it. Additionally, we inquired about a scooter rental at the front desk. The concierge said he would look into it and never followed up with us. The next morning we ordered orange juice and was charged $12 for one glass!! The only newspaper they offered could only be read in the lobby. After these bad experiences we tried to cancel our third night while we were in Antigua. The front desk kept on transferring me to a reservations line where no one picked up. Finally after asking to speak with the manager they said we could not cancel less then 72 hours before the stay. We explained that we already stayed there two nights at almost $400 a night and they still would not allow us to cancel without being charged. After arriving in San Juan for our third night in the city we were forced to return to the hotel since they already charged us. Once we got there we had to request the manager again and only after stressing that our stay was unpleasant and that we felt like we were being forced to stay at their crappy hotel did they credit us. This was all done in the lobby in front of other guests and I believe they only gave in because of this. I found this hotel on the Small Luxury Hotels of the World listings, the hotel claims to be a 4 star luxury hotel yet we were greatly disappointed due the poor treatment we received and the just average standard of the rooms. My advice is to skip out on El Convento it certainly is not worth the price and headache that awaits you.

<Author>oeil21
<Content>Beautiful Building The building was beautiful and in a wonderful location. Staff was great and free wine and cheese hour fantastic plus. Locals I knew before visiting go there for dinner or drinks and consider it one of the best on the island. Unfortunately the rooms were not that fantastic - they badly needed some updating and the bed was pretty uncomfortable. It was freezing in our room - we immediately turned the air off and opened the window but everyday housekeeping would pump it back up again. The bathroom was ok but definitely not four star.The linens seemed old and one night the bottom sheet came undone and I could feel the icky old matress pad with my feet! The tile was clean but the rugs I didn't want to walk on barefoot. Also if you rent a car better see what the hotel can do for you as far as parking goes. Its better to walk and take the free trolley around. If you rent a car there is a free shuttle from the rental company to the hotel - the front desk will arrange this for you.We were also under the impression breakfast was included but alas... it isn't. Check out the awesome breakfast places in the surrounding area that look like they have stayed the same since the 40's. The hotel serves seriously Americanized breakfast at New York prices.I think the building and staff was the biggest draw but might consider staying elsewhere next time. Definietly better than any large generic hotel along the beach. (They aren't that great anyway along the Atlantic...)

<Content>Lovely except for bedding, big deal to us My husband and I stayed there over a post-Xmas break. We found the desk staff doing triple duty, not informed, and overwhelmed (but very polite.) And, to boot, the mattress pad looked old and icky.I've never seen or felt anything like it in any classy hotel I've been in anywhere in the world. And if you are a Princess and the Pea person, you may be turned off by it too.I'd never sleep there again.

<Author>Phil6184
<Content>Nearly Perfect After reading the reviews Of the El Convento I must say my expectations were running high. I'm happy to report I was not dissappointed. The hotel is a Gem. The staff was excellent and the service near perfect. On arrival, I had a problem with the room's thermostat. One stop at the front desk solved that. Within 5 minutes a technician arrived and swapped out the faulty unit. The restaurants are just ok. The pool is tiny. But the many lounging alcoves and the unique setting make up for any slight deficiencies.About the only negative thing I can say is that the front desk seemed to have only one person working. Since it functions as concierge, reservationist, as well as front desk the lone worker is at times overwhelmed. This resulted in a dinner reservation request not being made until I made the request again. This isn't to say the staff was incompetant or uncaring, he was just overwhelmed. Management needs to pull someone from the back office at times when the front desk is so busy.Having said all this, I would return in a heartbeat.

<Author>midgetmama
<Content>El Perfecto! I stayed here December 21 at a total of $323 including tax.Our first encounter with the hotel was two days before our stay. We somehow ended up having to drive in Old San Juan (not very pleasant but amusing, nonetheless), and when we found the hotel, discovered there is no way to drive straight up to it to drop off our luggage. After driving around the block a few times, we finally decided to pull into the valet parking and ask if we could just leave the car for a moment while dropping off our luggage. We only spoke Spanish, so I'm not sure if that had any effect, but the valet said it would be no problem and ran in to get a porter while we unloaded the trunk. He never found one, so he brought our bags in himself. Checking them in was easy enough, although once again we were waiting for a porter to come to collect them, and that took some time. When he finally came, we tipped the valet and left at no charge for parking.Two days later when we checked in, that was quick and efficient. We were given our keys and all the information/maps we needed. We asked where the elevator was, so the front desk agent walked us to our room and showed us how to use the key in the elevator. She said the porter would be up shortly with our bags.We got the standard room, and it was lovely. The ceilings were high, decor was very different, and we had a nice view of the plaza outside. My mom was very excited she got to try out the Bose system she's wanted for so long. The plasma television had to be turned on by hand, and the buttons were hard to see since they are hidden, and the room was not well-lit. The remote controls everything else once it's on though.The bathroom was tiny but clean, although my mom said she saw some kind of mold/dirt in the vents in the door. The only real problem I had in the room was on the front door where either the handle or the lock (so unimportant I can't remember which) was sort of hanging off.1.5 hours later the porter finally showed up with our bags. Thank God we weren't in a rush! We each got a shower in, a long call to my sister and some television in the time we were waiting for him.The hotel grounds were beautiful, and we took lots of pictures of the Christmas decorations.We only stayed one night so didn't get to enjoy all the restaurants the hotel is so famous for, but we did have lunch at El Picoteo. We weren't hungry but really wanted to eat there, so I had a plate of manchego and a bowl of gazpacho while my mom had the grilled shrimp. She loved the paprika butter they served with bread, and the shrimp was very garlicky. My gazpacho wasn't quite as good as anything I've had in Spain, or even Cafe Ba-Ba-Reeba, but it was good enough, and the manchego was fantastic (as if you can ever go wrong with manchego). The ambience made for a nice ending to the trip, but the waiter was a little overly friendly. He kept standing behind a pillar and staring at me, so I figured it was the usual crush waiters always get on me. Then he awkwardly spoke in a very quiet voice, spending about 15 minutes telling us all about himself such as how it rained and he had to change his shirt that morning so he was late for work, and how he has to use a lot of Chapstick in Vegas. But he was gorgeous, so that made up for the awkward silences he forced us into.The porter returning our bags to us and bringing them out to the taxi was quite a bit quicker than our other experiences.The hotel was beautiful, all of the staff was friendly, and the food was delicious. We had a great time and would definitely recommend El Convento to anyone.

<Author>J&H74
<Content>Loved the El We usually prefer the Ritz or the Four Seasons, but decided to try El Convento to have a more authentic local experience. You could probably say that we are demanding and have high expectations. We were on a one-night stop over in San Juan. The choice was well worth it. The hotel exudes old world charm. Our room (508) overlooked the bay and the small plunge pool. It was small but acceptable. The hotel was refurbished in a manner which remains true to its era. The lobby was impressive with soaring ceilings and a patterned marble floor. The courtyard is lush with tropical vegetation and acres of terra cotta tile. While Old San Juan is very busy at night, the room was very quiet. We ate in the tapas restaurant on the second floor and the breakfast restaurant on the first floor. Both settings are in the courtyard and very romantic. The service was very good in both cases. We appreciated the morning newspapers (including the New York Times) that were available in the breakfast room. There was a pianist playing in the lobby salon at night. We ate at a nearby restaurant called Amadeus. It is within a short walk. The appetizers were great: corn fritters with mozzarella and dumplings. The main courses were bland and uninteresting. dessert was excellent: cheese flan. There was a good wine list. El Convento is located in the heart of Old San Juan. The area really comes alive at night. During the day, it is dominated by typical tourist shops. There are a couple of small legitimate antique shops but mostly the usual tourist stuff. The staff is very attentive and efficient.. The fitness center is small but has two treadmills, nautilus and some free weights. It is also open 24 hours a day The internet connection was excellent. What are the drawbacks? The hotel is in the middle of Old San Juan, so there is no beach. The traffic is heavy at all times of the day. Mosquitoes are thick and hungry鈥攑robably drawn by the fresh tourist meat and the lush vegetation. So like many hotels it is a question of your priorities and compromises. We were heading for the islands so a day without the beach was not a big issue.We would definitely return.

<Content>A very nice hotel We have just returned from a trip to this amazing hotel after a 2 week Caribbean cruise. The hotel is located in the heart of the old town near all the shops and restaurants. Our room was located on the 4th floor with views of the bay. <Author>NYC91
<Content>Great gem in the heart of the city My family and I stayed at the El Convento during the Thanksgiving holiday. The rooms were recently refurbished with quaint charm including color scheme, flat screen TVs, and Bose sound system. We had a great room-413, that overlooked the sea. Try to book this or rooms 410-414. The 4th floor is the best, in my opinion, as it has the pool and another open tanning/lounging area.The wine and cheese at 6 PM is great- great wine, great cheese.The pool is VERY small, MUCH smaller than it seems in the photos, but does the trick. Staying at the El Convento is like staying at a friend's house (or mansion). It's very comfortable, relaxed, and leisurely. The interior coutyard is amazing- like you're in Havana in the 50s. Amazing.Service is excelllent, with ONE exception. This terribly unpleasant woman at check-in. I didn't get her name, but everyone who encounters her knows who she is since she is the only one on staff with an attitude that does NOT flow with this hotel. Also, be aware that the beach is a cab ride away to the Mariott Courtyard if you want the typical tourist experience. And the BEST part, that no one tells you, is that the beach for the Mariott is located DIRECTLY across the street from the airport, making it EXTREMELY loud as planes take off and land. It's funny if you're in a good mood, and soooooo annoying if you're not.This has nothing to do with the El Convento property, more of an FYI.I could go on and on about the El Convento. You should definately stay here if you are looking for a European experience in the heart of the Carribean.

<Author>snmi47
<Content>The best of Old San Juan We had a great time on our honeymoon and stayed at the El Convento for two weeks. We stayed in room 217 which had high ceilings and a great little back terrace. The room was quiet, even though there were times with a variety of activity outside. The staff was very attentive, polite and patient with my broken Spanish, although everyone speaks English very well. The Old San Juan area is great to stay in and we'd explored a number of other hotels and found this to be the best authentic Puerto Rican experience with a great degree of class.I would advise against booking events through the hotel (unless you don't have a car) as they can add up quickly. We booked all of our activities individually and on our own (because we rented a car) and we covered the entire island. A must do is a trip to Vieques to see the bio-bay, but plan to stay overnight as the ferry does not run very often out of Farjardo.

<Author>Geanne
<Content>Old World Character/Modern Comforts El Convento is ideally located in the heart of Old San Juan, within easy walking distance of many outstanding historic sites, shops, restaurants and cafes. Our room was incredibly clean and comfortable, with plush bedding, a modern bathroom and flat-screen TV. Yet, the architectural details were beautifully preserved and the thick walls and high ceilings added to the room's authentically historic ambience. The design details throughout the hotel were stunning and there was no question of the building's architectural and historical significance. Internet access, a cozy library, self-service coffee throughout the day, and a daily wine and cheese hour helped make guests feel welcome. The hotel's tapas restaurant, El Picoteo, was fabulous. Our only regret was that we only had one meal at the tapas restaurant. El Convento is a one-of-a-kind gem of a hotel and we were grateful that its building has been so meticulously restored and that the hotel is so well managed.

<Author>juleve
<Content>A perfect escape for some city and civilization We live in the Caribbean, working at a very posh resort hotel in the British Virgin Islands. We took a week off in May and escaped to Puerto Rico to enjoy good food, Latin ambience, shopping, and above all, the staples of civilization: things like bookshops, cafes, and cinemas... which don't exist in the BVI.We stayed at El Convento the entire time and loved it. The hotel is beautiful with its central courtyard and the room was definitely unusual with its thick double wooden doors and high ceilings. We could definitely imagine the years of history the hotel had seen in its past life as a convent!The location was perfect. We loved Old San Juan and mostly stayed around there... took a taxi a few times to get to the Plaza de las Americas for shopping and cinema. We rented a car for two days as well to explore El Yunque rainforest and drove all around the island. The friendly staff at the hotel made the arrangements for us for the rental car - they also found us a men's barber shop!We weren't looking for beaches and were avoiding the sun since we get more than enough of that at home in the BVI (although I've heard that PR does have some great beaches - and its own virgin island is apparently extremely special).Next time I'm in Puerto Rico, I will definitely stay in El Convento again.

<Author>sej
<Content>Wonderful ambience Just got back from a stay at El Convento and thought about booking a return trip before we had even left! We had originally planned to stay in the Condado area but had heard about all of the construction going on so decided to switch home base to Old San Juan. After going to the Condado for dinner one night we realized what a good move we'd made. El Convento was a private, quiet respite in the middle of a town filled with architectual and sensual delights. At the beginning or end of a long day, what a treat it was to have a cup of coffee or tea while overlooking the indoor courtyard, town or bay. If you want constant action, casinos, etc., this isn't the place for you. As mentioned in other posts, it's tastefully presented and is definitely above average, but don't expect it to be comparable to a Ritz, Four Seasons or luxury boutique hotel. For example, the bathrooms are marble but they're small and are showing some wear. Our room was in good shape but other rooms had stained upholstery. For these reasons, I don't think the hotel is worth the rack room prices of $500 and up- which is why some people have been dissapointed. At those rates you expect luxury. We got a better price through a AAA discount. What you do get is personalized service from the moment you walk in, the best location of any of the hotels in town, and true Puerto Rican ambiance. Many of its surrounding streets are closed to tourist traffic at night which makes for nice walks (residents and hotel guests can still drive through). The free trolley service is the best deal in town. Get a current route map from one of the tourist centers (the hotel might have an outdated one). Take the trolley to specific locations (cruise ship docks, which are right in town) or ride it all the way around to get a great view of the town. The El Morro route is the best and goes by both forts. The portal to OSJ is right by the hotel. It leads to a pedestrian path by the bay that goes along the perimiter of the city- all the way to El Morro fort. We didn't use any of the in-house dining facilities, so can't comment on them. La Bombonera is the place the locals go for breakfast and pastries (I know, I used to live in P.R.). A freshly baked mallorca and a cup of strong Puerto Rican coffee is simply sublime! But don't go to Barrachina's for pina coladas. They tout themselves as being the originators of the drink but they're definitely not the best- tasted like pineapple juice and must have used colored water for rum since I didn't get my usual buzz. The best pina coladas are freshly mixed with cream of coconut, pineapple juice, rum and ice. If you see them using a mix, don't bother. If you have the time, things not to miss: the rainforest and architecturally beautiful Ponce. At Isla Verde Beach you can experince P.R. like a native. It's close to Old San Juan, has a bike/pedestrian trail along the beach, and is where you can get authentic Puerto Rican food in the shacks lining the road.  
<Date>Jul 17, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Charming! Very Special! Built around an open, interior courtyard, this lovely hotel brings the outdoor tropical ambience inside. Historic and very elegant public spaces. The rooms themselves are average, but everything else about this hotel is unforgettable!The hotel hosts an enjoyable complimentary wine and cheese reception in the early evenings between 6-7 pm. Coffee and tea are available all the time. A computer is availabe in a small library near the reception room.The staff are exceptionally nice and helpful. They really make you feel at home. There are three restaurants in and next door to the hotel. Breakfast is served in the courtyard--expensive, but worth the splurge at least once. As an alternative, there is a bakery about 3 blocks away that serves a good, inexpensive breakfast.El Convento is perfectly situated for sightseeing in Old San Juan. You can walk to everything. I just returned from a 2 night stay with my two college age daughters and they loved it as much as I did. All of us would recommend this hotel with considerable enthusiasm.

<Author>ejcrowe
<Content>Wish we'd had more time at El Convento I decided that spending our last night in Old San Juan after three nights on Vieques would be a good way of easing back into the hustle  bustle of the real world. Hotel El Convento is definitely more than we tend to spend on our hotel rooms, but I鈥檓 very glad we splurged. Resort-type places aside, it is the nicest full-service hotel I鈥檝e ever stayed in and I have to say that I would be hard pressed to stay anyplace else in OSJ in the future. The location is perfect for walking around, the courtyard of the hotel is a peaceful place to sit and enjoy a cup of coffee and a book in the early morning, and the views from the rooftop pool and decks were just lovely. Our room had two double beds, a flatscreen TV, a Bose CD player, small refrigerator, small safe, full bathroom, air conditioning, and a small Juliet balcony whose doors we could throw wide open to see the plaza right below us and the cathedral to our left. Every staff member, from the concierge to the bartenders to the bellhop exuded graciousness and made us feel welcome in a solicitous but not overbearing way. Included with the price of the room is an outdoor, early evening rooftop wine and cheese reception, which we were very glad to take advantage of. Our flight from Vieques was timed so that it would have been very difficult to eat an early lunch before hand, and our arrival at El Convento was such that their restaurant had stopped serving lunch already, and we did not want to eat a full meal at 3:45 pm, so the reception was ideal. The hotel provided a wide variety of hard and soft cheeses and other nibbles, plus a choice of about 6 different wines, an honor bar for those who want a cocktail, as well as coffee, tea, bottled water and soda. So the adults sat with our wine and martinis and our teenager with her soda as we watched a cruise ship leave port and saw the clouds to the west become tinted with the pastels of sunset.Check-out is at noon, but the hotel provides a secure closet for leaving behind luggage if, like us, you have a late afternoon flight and want to spend the time walking around OSJ. Guests who have already checked out can still take advantage of all of the hotel鈥檚 facilities, so we also had access to the pool but more importantly to the shower rooms in the fitness center so that we could change clothes before leaving for the airport. Our breakfast in the courtyard of the hotel was quite good, accompanied by excellent coffee, which my husband and I drank while waiting for our companions to join us. The fare was varied and priced in keeping with hotel鈥檚 prices. For our evening meal we walked down to Aguaviva, which served us some of the best seafood and cocktails we've ever enjoyed--the watermelon sangria was especially good. All in all, we loved Old San Juan and we hope to return sooner rather than later. The next time one of our flights to the Caribbean has a nasty layover (Grenada being the worse) we will definitely just plan to overnight in OSJ and stay at El Convento again.

<Author>kzdallas
<Content>A taste of the Old World in the Caribbean... We loved El Convento! This was my second time staying at El Convento and I would be thrilled to go again. It is a wonderful old hotel with a European atmosphere, personal service, modern conveniences (flat-screened tv, bose radio, fitness center, etc.), and the best location you could ask for in Old San Juan. You can easily walk from the hotel to all the historic sites in OSJ --El Morro, San Cristobal, the governor's house, San Juan Cathedral, the home of Ponce de Leon, etc.-- and to numerous shops and restaurants. There are duty free jewelry stores on every block, boutiques selling clothes and local handicrafts, outlet shops, and unusual and interesting art galleries. And the restaurants are superb. Most are small and unique. Dragonfly has incredible Latin-Asian fusion food (great sushi). The Parrot Club makes the best pork sandwich in the world -- and the Parrot Passion is quite refreshing! Agua Viva is open for lunch and dinner and serves good Latin inspired seafood (I loved the calamari sandwich and the big steel bowls of ceviche looked really tasty). Tantra is an exotic Latin-Indian restaurant, La Bombanero serves mallorcas fresh from the oven at breakfast time. This is a local spot which is more than 100 years old and looks like a cafe/diner/bakery combination...the coffee's great, too. Baru on San Sebastian Street is very good Mediterranean/Caribbean food and the Cafe Puerto Rico is good, cheap PR food. And the best tapas in the world are served at El Picoteo in the El Convento Hotel. We had a variety for dinner one night and had to go back the next day at lunch for more! They also make a superb Tres Leches cake and chocoloate mousse cake. You can have dinner at 7:00, hop in a cab and head to Isle Verde to the Casinos -- the Ritz, El San Juan, Intercontinental or many others -- and come back to El Convento afterward for coffee and dessert!The next time you have to change planes in San Juan to get to the Virgin Islands, Antigua, St. Martin, Aruba, Barbados...or other points south, think about a stopover in Puerto Rico. If you can only manage a day or two, stay at El Convento and enjoy Old San Juan. If you have longer, be sure to get out and explore the island. You shouldn't miss it!

<Author>tunneltravler
<Content>Beyond good! Charming, warm, spotless, well done, mysterious, all words to describe this wonderful small hotel. We wondered at the 200+ year old fruit tree in the inner courtyard, the beautiful oil paintings behind its massive wooden entry doors doors, and the tucked away terraces that have wonderful seating areas to steal conversation or to disconnect. Honor bar just a corner away from the roof top jacuzzi and small soaking pool that over looks the inner harbor. The tapas bar/restaurant El Picoteo is quality and a price to match. The rooms (opted for a partial harbor view) had ice cold A/C. It also had an exterior double door to let fresh air in if you like it tropical. Our double bed room had a nice semi-firm bed and pillows, marble bath, hot shower, frig, safe, iron, lots of hooks, free high speed internet, dimming floor lamps and lots of drawers and hangers. We stayed in Old San Juan because we're more city people in general and explore rural parts by car or other transport. But Puerto Rico being a beach island, we we're happy to find a courtesy pass that we could use to attend another resort's beach and facilities. At this time it's the Marriott Courtyard at Isla Verde (read: Muniz Airport). It's the antithesis of what we like in a hotel (but nice staff) and the beach was less than amazing. You could take a walk down to the public area where it was more crowded but overlooked a small island and seemed more scenic. The other way looked like any overbuilt ocean side city and a touch polluted, But that's not the El Convento's fault. You need to travel a ways to get to the beautiful beaches of P.R. if you're staying in San Juan. El Convento's staff was extremely helpful, fun and attentive. All in all I was very impressed. Put it on your list.

<Author>AKR1
<Content>Loved El Convento El Convento is an exceptional hotel with a great location in the absolute center of all the action in old San Juan. We were a family of four who stayed there last week and loved it. Our room turned out to be a big suite right next to the rooftop pool area and a staircase from there led us down to the patio area where they serve wine and cheese each evening. <Author>princeton12321
<Content>Take it for what it is Is this the Ritz Carlton? No. Does it pretend to be? No. This is an absolutely charming hotel located right in Old San Juan. Wonderful architecture and character you cant get in most places in San Juan. <Content>El Convento is absolutely terrific We loved this place. It's in a beautiful section of a fascinating city. It's not easy to taxi to because the traffic is awful and the streets are so narrower. However, the hotel is lovely inside  out  worth the crazy taxi drive. <Author>ScotTravller
<Content>Don't stay in room 324! Just returned from a weekend trip to San Juan (fri/sat night stay). The hotel has rustic charm and the staff were all very friendly (as were the other Puerto Ricans we met). However, make sure you don't stay in room 324. This room has an outlook onto the street and is very noisy. The hotel cafe which was just below and played loud music until it closed at 1am. The main problem was the bars and people in the street. The bar directly opposite was open until 5am (the time when i eventually got to sleep - for all of 3 hours). The next morning we complained and the staff were very accomodating and changed our room to one which although smaller was much improved. The staff seemed unsurprised by the complaint so i imagine this happens regularly.The other (minor) problem is that the hotel is right in the middle of old san juan which is great for walking about the streets but if you travel elsewhere and get a taxi back it can be difficult as the streets were jammed with cars. On the sat night we ended up getting dropped off by the taxi a few streets away and walking the rest (the taxi driver was very apologetic).This is a nice hotel (if a bit pricey) and the staff were helpful, just don't stay in 324!

<Author>tamiris
<Content>El Convento was wonderful! We recently spent 5 nights at the El Convento in Old San Juan. We loved everything about it - the location, the building, the service, the views from the terrace on the 3rd floor and the pool on the 4th. I would highly recommend it.Our room was very attractive, even though not very large and even though it did not have a lot of natural light. It had 6(!) lamps and/or wall sconces, which we appreciated since we like to read. There was turn down service every evening. The bathroom was not large, but nice. The room opened onto an arcade going around the courtyard in the middle of the building, which had been a convent. There were trees, plants, etc. in the courtyard, including fruit bats flying around in the evening (they stayed in the courtyard and did not fly into the outdoor corridor. Every evening they lit candles on small tables set up overlooking the courtyard.There are 3 restaurants in the building, one in the courtyard, one on the 2nd floor overlooking the courtyard, and another on the 2nd floor near the side entrance of the building (which is onto the 2nd floor, since it is built on a hill.Every night from 6-7 pm there was complimentary wine and cheese on the terrace on the 3rd floor. We enjoyed talking to other guests there.Old San Juan is small and you can walk everywhere from the hotel. I would love to return some day.

<Author>suzyjacuzzi
<Content>Enchanting Hotel We spent 3 nights at the El Convento after traveling to other places in the Caribbean. The hotel is centrally located for exploring Old San Juan. Our very clean and tastefully decorated room was on the 5th floor with wonderful views and (to my husband's surprise) a really nice flat screen tv! The staff at the hotel was friendly and very accommodating. We were pleasantly surprised by Old San Juan and cannot wait to return. We spent 2 nights just walking around eating tapas and drinking our way thru the city. There is a very good Tapas restaurant right in front of the El Convento through the courtyard - I would highly recommend for a casual lunch (try their Sangria). We went to the Ritz Carlton one night to check it out but really wish we had just stayed right in Old San Juan - so much to see and do. I would go back to Old San Juan in a heartbeat, the nonstop flights from the States and the approximately to the airport makes Old San Juan and easy getaway destination.

<Author>Miner1
<Content>Like the curate's egg - good in parts El Convento has the possibility of being one of the great hotels, but is let down by needless inefficiencies. Its position, architecture and ambience are superb, but there are too many problems, individually small but adding up.We stayed for three nights in November. Like other previous respondents we arrived at a reasonable time to find no room available, nor any forecast as to when one would be. Eventually, at about 4pm we were given the keys to a room which was not made up. This was quickly remedied but annoying. No complaint about the reception and concierge who were pleasant. The new room was satisfactory, although not large.Again like many others, we found the lift out of order one day.The barman at the Tapas bar was downright unpleasant, although we were later informed that this bar is not part of the hotel. Best avoided, there is plenty of choice in the area. The main hotel restaurant was adequate and although not inspiring the staff were pleasant and efficient.The maid service left something to be desired with heavy dust in some areas.Other complaints were they lost our laundry (found eventually), and the telephone did not work. When we did manage to make a call, the pen did not work!However, that did not mean we did not enjoy our stay. Staff at the front desk was always helpful, especially Carmen, and other staff were always pleasant. The design and ambience of the hotel are stunning, at the centre of a beautiful historic city. The complimentary bar between 6 and 7pm is a lovely idea, and although the pool is small, the deck area has a beautiful aspect and is a pleasant place to relax.We still think this is the best place to stay in Old Sann Juan, but just wish they would get their act together.We booked through expedia.co.uk at a reasonable rate with no problems.

<Author>pman38
<Content>Could have been better My wife and I stayed at the El Convento for two days prior to a cruise. We selected the hotel, as we like Old San Juan and were pretty much able to walk anywhere to shop or dine. We were celebrating our tenth wedding anniversary. We had booked the room through the cruiseline. Upon checking in after a long day, we were told the only room available had twin beds. We explained that we had requested a room with a queen sized bed. They stated they had no other rooms, but would try to get us another room the next day. I am not sure where the mixup took place. I did contact the cruiseline who stated a queen sized bed was requested. ???? We had to take the room. Upon retiring for the night, the toilet in the room overflowed all over. We had not even used the toilet as of yet. Water was everywhere. We called the front desk and they sent a maintenance person up. It took him awhile, but apparently he fixed whatever caused the problem. After he left, the toilet started running and making very strange noises, and would not stop. I called the front desk irate, as it was late, and we were very tired. Miraculously, another room became available after we were told earlier there was nothing available. The person at the front desk stated this room also had twin beds. We immediately took the room, as we were very tired. This room was OK but the hotel really needs to do some upgrading, especially in the rooms. Obviously plumbing is an issue as well. The following day the front desk called and stated a room with a queen sized bed became available, as someone had cancelled. We declined, as we did not feel like packing everything up again. On a positive note, the wine/cheese reception each night was outstanding. A nice assortment of cheeses and wine. Cafe Bohemio was excellent as well. One last note. The hotel is all open. We do prefer at times to be in air conditioning, as the heat bothers us at times. The only place we found air conditioned areas was in the rooms. All dining areas are in the open. Ceiling fans are present, however. We will stay at another hotel on our next visit to San Juan.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent experience at El Convento My wife an I stayed at the El Convento for 3 nights during our honeymoon. This was the last leg of our trip after spending a week over at St. Johns and we were not disappointed. The service was stellar... The woman at the front desk (can't recall her name but she had braces :)) had taken note that it was our honeymoon, congratulated us and then put us in what many considered the best room in the house on the 5th floor. Since this was the first time someone actually really acknowledged with some excitement on us being newlyweds and went out of their way to find a great room, make us reservations on the spot for dinner, etc... it really meant a lot to us and really set the tone for the rest of our stay - great service. The room itself (I *think* 508) had been featured in many magazines with two windows/doors that had a view of the bay and also the pool area. The room was extremely tasteful and well thought out in terms of color scheme, decorations and furniture... along with being extremely clean. On our first night we took advantage of a pre-dinner snack at the nightly free cheese and wine hour only to come back to our room afterwards to find our bed turned down with rose pedals put into the shape of a heart on our bed (very nice touch). Several moments later there was a knock on our door with a bottle of champange and truffles. The inner courtyard was very nice, with breakfast in the morning and a tappas bar overlooking looking it - which ended up being our favorite place for drinks and snacks as the food was excellent. The location of the hotel itself in Old San Juan is perfect with walking distance to the shops and several execellent restaurants. If you want to go a bit further there is always a taxi out front. One night we took a taxi over to the Sheraton at Isle Verde for dinner and the casino, 15 minute ride at about $18, a little expensive but still reasonable. We would definitely stay again (in fact already setting up our next trip) and have absolutely nothing negative to say about the hotel or service of the resort... and I consider myself picky. Two thumbs up.

<Content>I agree with Victor of New York The hotel is absolutely beautiful and the location cannot be beat! Everything you could possibly want or need are right here, practically on your door step. Having said all that, we were moved from a standard room to a junior suite on our second night here even though we booked for a deluxe room (which is a really nice bonus). Unfortunately it is the suite that is leaking but wild horses wouldn't drag us out of here for the space!The Tapas bar at the hotel is very good and has great ambience. We have not tried Cafe Bohemio.You can visit the Barcardi Rum Distillery by catching a ferry from Pier 2 at the waterfront (5 minute walk from El Convento) to Catano ($0.50) and take a taxi to the Distillery ($3.00). All in all a great experience with few disappointments.

<Author>shannyh1
<Content>The Hotel Elconvento My husband and I just returned from a trip to Puerto Rico, staying 6 nights at the Hotel Elconvento...October 10-16th. After booking our room through Travelocity, we had a bit of a problem when we arrived in that the staff stated our room was a superior instead of the deluxe booked. Upon showing them proof, we were happily given room 501. During our first night, San Juan experiened more than average rainfall and our room had a couple leaks (one in the bathroom and one from the ceiling); Also we were unable to make telephone calls to the US mainland through the telephone system from the rooms. We informed the desk of our problems of leakage and were cheerfully transferred to room 510, which had a better view of San Juan Bay. This room was very satisfactory and nicely appointed with it's decor. Our CD player did not work, however. The room was clean and comfortable.Dining at The Elconvento was a bit 'iffy' as the Bistro was closed for refurbishing. We enjoyed our breakfast each morning in the inner courtyard (when it was not raining)..however, breakfast was a bit high-priced ($39 for two of bacon and eggs, toast, juice and coffee). There were a few times the lift did not work as well. We are assuming that the heavy rains were responsible for the malfunction.The pub, El Picateo was lovely and offers not only drinks but light snacks such as tappas and sandwiches. In the evening dinners are available as well. Rich Puerto Rican music wafts through the bar and restaurant sitting.From 6-7PM is free wine/cheese offerings. The cheeses were nothing special, however, the many wines were lovely. The corridors are lovely and the terraces are beautifully lit. Many different plants, flowers, and trees line the hallways and terraces, giving a romantic air to the hotel.The swimming pool and hot tub are very small, but clean and there is ample area for sunning. There is a lovely view from the swimming area as well as the terraces.There is free internet access in the library.Hotel Elconvento is centrally situated nicely in Old San Juan and in convenient walking distance to all attractions. The city is very hilly, so wear comfortable footwear! Just a few blocks away from the hotel is a trolley (small bus) that will transport you throughout the city for free. There is no need to rent a car if Old San Juan is where you are going to stay for the entire trip. We hired a driver for one day to take us on a tour, visit the Bacardi Rum Distillery, and treated us to an authentic Puerto Rican restaurant for lunch. The cost of this was $120 for 5 hours. There were other tours the concierge desk (same people as the front desk) offers, but dont hesitate to ask to make up your own package. They are most accommodating.All in all, we found the Hotel Elconvento staff very helpful and friendly. For a 350 year old building, it is well maintained and has more than enough staff to meet your needs. We were a bit disappointed by the housekeeping staff. They made up the bed each day, but towels were not replaced as needed.I think in the future we would not stay an entire 6 days in Old San Juan, but visit the beaches in Ponce and other areas of interest.  
<Date>Oct 27, 2005

<Author>sahman
<Content>Tranquility, and free wine One always takes a risk when booking a hotel, sight unseen, in an unknown town. Staying at El Convento made me look like an genius. The hotel is a large, romantically lit facade set on a small plaza. The setting is romatic, relaxing, and a fabulous respite from the busy town, despite being a 2 minute walk from good shopping, art galleries and restaurants. My wife and I particularly enjoyed the daily wine and cheese offering. It provides a unique opportunity to meet other guests, and watch the sun set before going out on the town. The service was very good, without being obtrusive, and the rooms clean and comfortable, with high ceilings. Each room has a small cafe table outside the front door, looking out on the central atrium. I'd highly recommend this hotel if you are more of a city person than a beach person, however the beach is a quick cab ride away. Definitely a great alternative to the cookie-cutter resort hotels.

<Content>best option for diverse san jaun el convento has an excellent location for a city tour of san jaun -- walking distance to excellent shops, restaurants  clubs. the property is charming and historic, although could use renovation to bring it back to 4-star standards. we found the staff very friendly and able to answer our questions and give excellent advice on shopping, clubs, restaurants, etc. el convento is no where near a beach. however, a $16 cab ride gets you to their sister property on isla verde -- which is a wide, clean, safe beach with lots of ammenities. the pool at conventro is small, esp when any children decend and start splashing water into your adult beverage. the rooms and bathrooms nice. overall, convento is a better alternative to the Ritz Carlton. the Ritz was quite crowded and a little worn -- certainly not what I expected hearing it was 5-star.

<Author>MrTetley
<Content>Sheer Brilliance Okay, so this next line may sound conceited, but: growing up, I was lucky to stay in some of the world's best hotels. We'd watch Lifestyles of the Rich and Famous, read lists of the best, and say, 'Been There, Been There.' Well, I may've been a student traveller between then and now, but this place ranks as one of the absolute best I've been to.I was only there for two days, one night, but oh how I wish it was longer. It was, no less, the last night of our honeymoon, and we'd had a lovely week in the BVIs on the beach, and were sad to leave, but El Convento was brilliant.Every staff member was great. Fantastic bellboy (Gadrial, I think was his name), great check-in, restaurant staff were great. And the room was lovely. So many nice touches, like the tables and chairs with candles outside the rooms in the hall, the gorgeous courtyard, the views, the location, etc. Almost best of all, though, was their lovely convention of having a free wine and cheese affair every afternoon from 6-7. open bottles of good wine, nice cheeses, and you could go to town. And their honor bar was also a nice way of telling their guests that they're different from the rest.The tapas restaurant (El Picoteo) was lovely looking, and had some nice stuff. My wife and I had a great meal, and woke the next morning feeling truly blessed to have stayed there. We stayed at the Water Club on the way out to the BVIs, but this was so much better. Go there.

<Author>TresSirenas
<Content>Absolutely the Best! As an owners of a small Inn on the West Coast of Puerto RIco, we often travel to San Juan for a quick getaway, having stayed in the many hotels in Condado and Isle Verde, our absolute favorite place to visit is the El Convento! On our most recent visit, traveling with friends from Europe who also own a BB in the south of France, and our children, we took 4 rooms, after finding a great rate on the internet. The architecture and ambience exemplify the charm of old San Juan, the rooms ar decorated to reflect the Spanish influence, and the service is unsurpassed. We especially enjoy the wine happy hour with a great variety of cheeses and fruit, offered every night, complimentary on their terrace overlooking the old city. After enjoying a great dinner at one of the many fine restaurants, this last visit Perigino's, fantastic, we enjoy their roof top pool for a swim under the stars before retiring. We often reccomend to our guests arriving in San Juan to stay at the El Convento before traveling to the west coast. It's no wonder this hotel is rated #1 by tripadvior, it clearly deserves it. To anyone visiting our beautiful Isalnd, before you head to the beaches, spend one or two nights first here, you won't regret it!

<Author>forestwind
<Content>Surprising Stumbles for a Great Hotel We had a great deal of trouble checking in. The first woman was not very smart. We were sent out for lunch. Then told it would be another hour. Then another two hours. At 4 o'clock, we were really hot and uncomfortable. We demanded they find a room or find us another hotel. A pleasant and competent woman took over, got us a room on the 4th floor facing the tiny pool. We liked our room. However, the next problem arose because we asked the front desk to find us a day tour of El Yunque. We were told it would cost more to use a credit card, it would cost more because the minibus had to go out of its way to pick us up. We agreed to $50 a person. The minibus was on time and the trip was fine. But on the way back we learned that others were charged $40 apiece, that they wanted to go to the airport immediately (with us in tow), and the driver did not have credit card slips (and first denied accepting credit card), then he put $55 on the bill for each of us! Well, we left the minibus in Condado to avoid the airport, we got a cab back to El Convento, and we demanded to know how El Convento could have chosen to deal with such a tour outfit. We never received a reply. El Convento has an obligation to look after its guests by choosing to deal with reputable tour organizers.

<Author>JuliusNomad
<Content>Excellent hotel, full of old world charm El Convento was the perfect place for my wife and me to stay for the first night of our honeymoon. We also got a good price through Hotels. We arrived early at 12pm and mentioned to the front desk that this was the first night of our honeymoon; they were very courteous and put us in a lovely room (#519) on the top floor which has the biggest private terrace in the hotel. In the evening when we returned from dinner and our paseo (evening stroll) we found on our bed a large heart-shape made out of rose petals, with a rose in the middle and two chocolates, together with a card welcoming us and wishing us well. When we were walking out of the room in our bathrooms (heading for the pool) we discovered an ice bucket with a bottle of champagne and two glasses -- a very thoughtful gesture from the night manager. The hotel itself is beautiful and charming, located in the middle of Old San Juan, adjacent to a large church and beautiful square, and a short walk along blue tinted cobblestones and Havana-like street scenes to historic buildings and boutique stores. We mentioned our plan to travel the next day to the islands of Culebra and Vieques (collectively known as the 鈥淪panish Virgin Islands鈥? located about 30 miles west of the US Virgin Island of St Thomas) -- Carlos at the front desk quickly called Avis for us and arranged for hotel pickup to their car rental office, securing a competitive price of $58 (including tax) for a one way rental to Fajardo. This rate is slightly lower than the $60-70 you pay if you travel by taxi, and allowed us to visit the rain forest en route. Lastly, we should mention the complementary wine and cheese in the evening -- which gave us the opportunity to mingle with other guests and look out from the third floor to the church -- and complementary breakfast. We greatly appreciate the excellent and thoughtful service of the staff of El Convento; they made our visit truly memorable.

<Author>dm2123
<Content>A lovely hotel, believe the reviews My husband and I just returned from a lovely stay at the Hotel El Convento.This was a suprise trip for my birthday and was originally set for a stay at the Water Club, but after reading other traveler's horror stories we changed the reservation to El Convento. I could not have been happier. The hotel is very charming and conveniently located in Old San Juan. We checked in at 12:30 am and our room was ready, the bed had been turned down for us and soft music was playing upon our entrance to the room. Our room was on the fifth floor, which is the highest floor and had a nice view of the city, the bay and mountains in the distance. The room was very clean, as well as the bathroom. The food in the hotel was excellent. I did have one gripe and please ask the hotel about this before choosing a room.There was a very large wedding in the hotel on Saturday night. The noise during the wedding reception was not nearly as bad as afterwards. Our room was located somewhat near the elevator and by the pool area (which is on the fourth floor). The wedding guests brought their party to the hallways and the pool area and loudly carried on until 5:30 am. The air conditioner was a bit noisy, so it thankfully drowed out some of the noise, but it was a bit ridiculous. So, I suggest if there is any function, such as a wedding in the hotel, ask for a room towards the back of the hotel to avoid a possible sleepless night. I know some people have commented about the pool being extremely small. Well, it is, but we happened to be the only people there most the time. On Sundays, you can hear parishioners singing spanish hymns in the church across the street if you are on the pool deck. Our room also had doors that opened up to a mini terrace, and we were treated to live music from a nearby festival. I definitely reccomend this hotel - the staff was very polite, and you really are in the middle of all the action. I swear by the reviews on this site, so thank you for the all the reviews that helped me choose and experience this nice hotel. Happy travels.  
<Date>Jul 2, 2005

<Author>Piolina
<Content>Charming, perfect location! We just came back from San Juan and stayed one night at El Convento. Our assigned room wasn't ready and they moved us to the top floor, one of the best rooms with fabulous views of the city, right above the pool area. I loved the details: bottled water in the fridge, bath robes and high speed internet. Plus, the wine and cheese reception was exceptional. But the best of all was that they filled our room with rose petals because they knew we were celebrating our anniversary. That was priceless! The only negative things I could say are that the room and bathroom weren't exactly clean, the A/C was not working in the morning due to maintenance and we were told breakfast was not included in our rate (although most reviews here talked about free breakfast). But, I must say that we got a really good rate through their website and I cannot complain for what we got. The hotel is beautiful, the staff is friendly and the location is unbeatable. I would definitely stay there again and I would recommend it to anyone wanting to stay in the Old San Juan!

<Content>Elegant and enchantingl I recently stayed at Hotel El Convento for six nights. I found it to be an enchanting visit. The hotel is unique, historic and beautiful. Right across from the cathedral and in the historic quarter of Old San Juan, the hotel offers beautiful architectural detail, a service oriented staff and a setting that is relaxing and elegant. My room was quite comfortable with a view that looked out over Fortaleza (Govenors's Mansion). The pool, though small, offered a wonderful view of Old San Juan and the port. The interior of the hotel was historic with beautiful marble floors, furniture and art. The courtyard below was lush and shaded by a magnificant tree. On the thrid floor terrace there was a wonderful outdoor patio which served as a great place to read and relax as well as a library room with internet access. Each night at 6:00 Hotel Convento has an incredible wine and cheese gathering for guests. So nice to visit with new friends each night and the wine and cheese was quite generous. The staff were wonderful and gracious. Every effort is made to meet guests needs and make them feel comfortable. And each night, your bed is turned down and wonderful choclates on the pillow. I found the Hotel Convento to be a delightful and magical.James
