<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>positives exceed negatives I own a small historic inn and I like to stay at historic properties when I travel. I spent two weeks El Convento; long enough to get a real feel for the place. Here's what I found. You can't beat the location if the ambiance of the old city is what you're looking for. I stayed in a room on the second floor overlooking the square in front of the hotel. The room was large and had a ceiling that must have been twenty feet high! I loved it. (rooms on the third and fourth floors were added to the top of the old convent and don't have quite the same antique feel as the second floor) The room was clean, the bed comfortable, the bath small, but more than adaquate. The maid service was good, twice a day, and I really appreciated the in-room internet connection for my laptop. I found the staff to be genuinely freindly and helpful. I would have no problem recommending the hotel for a stay of any length. However, my stay was not without a few problems. I read other reviews that mention faulty airconditioning. Mine worked but was very noisy. I suspected a bent fan blade hitting a shroud, the sort of thing that can be fixed with a screwdriver. I reported it, a repairman came promptly, agreed with the diagnosis, but claimed to be unqualified to fix it. He promised the regular maintenance crew would be in the next day and take care of it. They didn't come that day or any other. After a week of excuses I used a coin to remove the screws holding the grill, reached in and fixed it myself. Noise can be a problem. Most rooms are situated away from the busy street but noise echos around the small streets easily. My room was fitted with an extra window pane that cut down the noise but did not eliminate it. A bigger problem was the Hotel's practice of renting ground floor space for wedding receptions and other functions on the weekends. The noise from one party did not end until after one AM. I would recommend a set of ear plugs just in case.These annoyances aside, I enjoyed my stay and would stay again.  
<Date>May 28, 2005

<Author>klbozeman
<Content>Like a setting from an old movie! My husband and I stayed here after a cruise in early May. From the moment we arrived, we were absolutely amazed by the beauty of this place, both in the public areas and in the guest rooms themselves. The history of this hotel, with its beginnings as a convent and its many different incarnations as hotels over the years, only adds to its charm. This is definitely one of the best hotels we've ever stayed at, and we hope to return very soon! Unlike other reviewers, we experienced truly outstanding service and had no problems at all with our room, which featured Spanish tile floors, British Colonial-style furniture, and a charming window with floor-to-ceiling shutters that swung open and let you peer out over a flower-filled window box onto the cobblestone street below.But the most outstanding feature of the hotel has to be the courtyard, a lush tropical space filled with flowers and an incredibly old tree right in the center. Many of the buildings in Old San Juan have these types of courtyards, but of all the ones we saw, the one at the El Convento was the most beautiful. There are 2 restaurants situated right in the courtyard itself. We had a delicious lunch under an umbrella at one of them, El Picoteo, and ate tapas while sipping pina coladas, which were invented in San Juan. The location of the hotel is also ideal--right across the street from the historic Cathedral of San Juan. (From the hotel pool deck balcony, we sat and heard the sounds of Spanish-language hymns wafting from the cathedral's open doors during a Saturday evening mass.) It's also within easy walking distance of the El Morro fort and all the rest of the great attractions in Old San Juan.The front desk staff was helpful and friendly, allowing us to check in at 11 a.m., well before the stated check-in time, and telling us about events that were happening in the area that weekend. They were also a big help when we had to check out at 5 a.m. to catch a flight; there was no trouble getting a taxi or a bellman to help with luggage. Along with the many churches and governmental buildings, the El Convento is on all of the tourist maps as a bona fide tourist attraction in Old San Juan, but if you are visiting San Juan for its colorful history and charm, go one better and book a room here as your home base.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Definetly not luxury treatment Ok, where to start? The El Convento is a lovely hotel in historic Old San Juan, from a visual perspective. It is ideally located for walking around Old San Juan, close to many shops, restaurants, and historic sites. They also have a very nice daily wine and cheese tasting, as well as a nice complimentary continental breakfast in the morning. Unfortunately, for a hotel priding itself on being a member of the small luxury hotels of the world category, it fails to live up to those expectations of luxury when it comes to service.We arrived as a post-cruise package around noon, and were told that our rooms weren't quite ready yet and were told to check back in about an hour. That one hour turned into over 3 hours, as rooms were not ready until after 3 pm. The rooms themselves were large and roomy, with a nice-sized bathroom as well. The room my wife and I were given had a malfunctioning air conditioner, (there was also another member in our party whose air conditioning was not working) something we did not bring to the concierge's attention due to us just being so tired the first day, we took a long nap that night. When we did notify the front desk the following morning around 8 am as we were getting ready to go out for the day, we were told that they would get maintenance to check it out. When we returned to the hotel in mid-afternoon, the air conditioning was still not working. When I called again, the concierge said she would speak to her supervisor very quickly and then call me right back. Thirty minutes later after I called them again (and about 10 minutes after my wife had gone down to the desk to speak to them again about the air conditioning), we were told that they would assign us a different room.After 3 different calls to let the porter know we were ready to have our luggage taken to the new room, we were finally situated in a room with temperature control. It seems like a minor irritation, but they (a) either didn't check it out at all after we originally asked them to, or (b) knew it wasn't working and weren't going to do anything about it until we pestered the front desk staff enough.Our check out problems were the the biggest problems, though. Checking out itself wasn't a problem, but catching our taxis to the airport with all of our luggage was another situation. We checked out of the hotel at noon, and had arranged for our luggage to be held (with claim checks) until 1 pm for our transport to the airport. Taxis didn't arrive until closer to 1:30, and only when we got to the airport did we realize that we were missing 2 bags still, one my wife's, one belonging to my sister. My sister had to ride back to the hotel with the taxi driver to pick up the missing luggage, which the hotel staff told her was left on a chair by where we were sitting waiting for the taxis, as though we left them behind and forgot to grab them. I'm still trying to figure out how this could be since they were bags that had been checked in with the porter staff and once we gave the bags to them, they never left their custody. Its obvious that they forgot to pull them when they loaded the taxis, regardless of the excuse they offered of where they found the bags.My best advice for anyone looking to stay at El Convento? Visually pleasing, and ideally located if you want to stay in Old San Juan. However, the quality of service is severly lacking and very indifferent. I'm sure that for the price, you can find better accomodations elsewhere in San Juan, especially in the Isla Verde area. If and when my wife and I return to San Juan, our accomodations will definetly be elsewhere other than El Convento. *Note: This hotel was booked by our travel agent, who acknowledged beforehand she was not strongly familiar with San Juan and its accomodations*

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I Love This Place and I can't stop thinking about it since I've been back home. I have a completely different view of old San Juan having seen it both at sunset and sunrise and I'll be going back vey soon.If you'e looking for a slick style delivery like only what's ordinarily the product of one of the bigger hotel chains this place is probably not for you. I mean my TV remote didn't work and I also heard what might have been a neighboring toilet flush very early in the morning and to some of you those two things alone might be enough for a deal breaker but El Convento is so beautiful and interesting and soothing that frankly I didn't much care about either. So if you want something different but very upscale, literary without being snobbish, if you want to see how really beautiful and sleepy old San Juan is early in the morning or you would enjoy reading at the end of the day on the veranda underneath the shaded rawd iron gazebo enjoying an afternoon coffee or tea while overlooking the 400 year old pastel yellow Cathedral of San Juan you'd love the El Convento Hotel.I'll be back . . . I loved the room, the food, the privacy, the tapas bar, the ambiance, how the palm trees and lush foliage played with the light all day long providing the most interesting spaces throughout the property. I loved the multi level terraces, the colorful flowers and that beautiful little square right outside. If I could make one request it would be that maybe a few vegan or macrobiotic type dishes would be added to whats already a delicious menu just so people who really like to eat light or smart or vegan can find lets say a soy burger or veggie burger or mahi mahi burger or a seitan or tempeh dish. No need to make a big deal about it but it would be great to know its there . . . and I bet many of your guests would like to have a chnage of pace every now and then. I think if you keep in mind what the El Convento Hotel is and more importantly what it is not, you'll have an unforgettable experience staying there.

<Author>EmilieV7
<Content>Relaxed sophistication, great service My husband and I stayed here in March when our flight to Guadeloupe was cancelled and we found ourselves stuck in San Juan for a night. Our stay could not have been nicer. From the moment we arrived we loved this place. Gorgeous hotel with soaring ceilings, Spanish arches and a stunning courtyard around which the rooms are built. This place manages to combine the best of old world elegance with contemporary style. And, the added bonus is that the service from all staff we encountered (including waiters in the restaurant) was efficient, warm and hospitable. We arrived about 10:30 PM starving and were delighted with the tapas restaurant. The rooms are a tad on the small side but the ambiance, service and sheer good taste more than compensate. We will definitely go back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Save your money and stay elsewhere We recently stayed at this hotel on the recommendation of a relative that lives locally. The room was clean, but smaller than anticipated. The first night went fine, but the second night (Thursday) there was booming music until the early morning hours from the bar/restaurant on the property. We requested a room change the 3rd night and were pleased with a larger room in the quieter part of the hotel. The gym consists of a couple of tread mills, some older cardio equipment and a weight room. Hardly worthy of mention.The problems with this hotel were as follows:1) We had them book a tour for us and were told we would be picked up at 8:45 am. At 9:15, still no sign of our tour, so we went inside to inquire. As it turned out, the tour company called the previous day to say they would not be coming until 9:30 and OOPS! the hotel lost the message. An hour of our precious vacation time wasted.2) We asked the hotel to transfer our luggage from the 1st room to the 2nd room while we were out for the day. When we got back from the beach, all we wanted was a hot shower, but we had no clothes to change into. We called the front desk to inquire about our bags, and were assured they were on their way. 15 minutes later, no bags, a second call. They're coming. 15 minutes later, I walked downstairs and got my own bags and hauled them upstairs myself.3) They did offer a decent continental breakfast, but some of the wait staff was inhospitable. Overall, first, I would expect better service for the price. Second, while the hotel was very cute, historical, and well situated, it wasn't worth the price we paid. Save your money and stay in Isla Verde or Condado. It will be money well spent.  
<Date>Mar 16, 2005

<Content>Service needs MAJOR work Where do I begin? Overrun with cruise passengers and fully booked during our two nights there, the problems just never ended. An incomplete list: No vouchers provided for breakfast, even though we had pre/post cruise package [which stated breakfast included, but failed to disclose that gratuities on breakfast were extra]. Old San Juan sorely needs a competitor to this place, in the same category. They've clearly sold out to the lucrative cruise ship add-on market, and the zoo-like atmosphere this creates, with resulting lapses in service, over and over.

<Content>Beautiful, quiet, luxurious....small rooms We stayed at El Convento from February 22-24, 2005. We got a good deal on hotels ($180 per night) and decided to splurge. Check-in was fast, concierge announced we'd gotten an upgrade (cool!) to a partial suite. Our room was 305, and wow was it gorgeous. Two full-length windows looking out on the cathedral plaza, an inlaid-marble dining table with six chairs, several cushy chairs, tv, fridge, sideboard, buffet table, two coffee tables, two chandeliers...it was a large, very medieval-atmosphered suite. There were even tapestries and real candles. The bathroom was small but all marble. But then we noticed the bed--the sofa had been pulled out into a full-size sofa bed. We tried to open the door we assumed went into the bedroom, but it was locked--and we realized what partial suite meant--the doors had been closed and someone else was being rented the bedroom part of the suite for the night. The sofa bed was rather lumpy and small, but we liked the rest of the room so much we decided to deal with it. (We slept terribly, since we both kept falling to the sunken-in middle of the bed). And the person in the room on the other side was laughing along with her tv, so my husband and I had a loud conversation about the weather so she'd realize we could hear her and she quieted down. So that was the only drawback, but we did choose to keep that room rather than switch to another, because we had seen several of those other rooms on the way in, and could tell from that and from the floor plan on our room door that the vast majority of the rooms are quite small, though nicely furnished. The complimentary breakfast included juice, fruit plate, hot or cold cereal, and basket of breads and danishes--much more than we could eat--served in the beautiful courtyard. The 6-8 pm wine and cheese reception is awesome: 8 wines, crackers, 4 cheeses, grapes--we didn't go out for dinner that night because we filled up on their delicious (and free) offerings, which we ate on the rooftop terrace by the pool, listening to the fountains and watching the stars. Even though the hotel is on a plaza, it's so very quiet! And the complimentary water bottles and tea and coffee available at all hours from the lounge area on the third floor was fantastic. Free internet access computer use there too. (Ask for a room on the third floor so you'll have easiest access to all this.)We ate in the hotel's Spanish tapas restaurant, the sangria was amazing, the tapas ok, but very convenient courtyard location after a full day of flying. The concierge was very helpful with suggesting other places to eat, as she had a large book full of restaurant menus. In all, highly recommend, but be prepared for small rooms. The complimentary extras here make all the difference--take advantage of the wine  cheese reception, and the breakfast, and the lounge area, and enjoy the decadent step back in time.  
<Date>Mar 8, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful ambience, service needs work We just spent 5 nights at El Convento (Dec. 28 - Jan 2). For starters, the location is perfect, and we loved the atmosphere of the hotel. It was very peaceful, our 4th floor room had a lovely view, and we enjoyed twice daily maid service, lounging on the pool deck (never crowded) and the evening wine and cheese.However, customer service left a lot to be desired. We booked online through the hotel website and received an email confirmation. However, when I called El Convento to confirm, they had no record of our reservation. If you book online, definitely make sure you confirm with the hotel as well! We too found the concierge to be incompetent. We called multiple times before our trip to inquire about New Years Eve reservations and were told they would be taken care of, but this was never done. The concierge was unable to recommend restaurants to us, and many times told us reservations were made when in fact they weren't. We found the concierge to be the biggest disappointment at El Convento, expect to do research and make arrangements yourself.Despite this, the positives of the hotel outweight the negatives, and we would stay at El Convento again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best in Old San Juan We stayed at the El Convento for 5 nights (December 6-11, 2004). We were pleasantly suprised upon our arrival and our experience only got better from there. We stayed on the 4th floor and had a nice view of the bay. The room was clean and very quiet, and well kept during our stay. We were amazed that we couldn't hear any noise from outside the room. Our room was nicely furnished and the bathroom was very nice as well. The hotel jacuzzi/pool area was convenient and not busy, offering a good view. The evening wine/cheese gathering was wonderful including outdoor seating and view of Old San Juan and the streets below. We got a good room rate on LuxRes. Our only disapointment was that the breakfast that had been advertised to be part of the room rate was no longer included, with no apologies from the staff. But, our in-room fridge came in handy for our own breakfasts overlooking the courtyard. We really enjoyed our stay here. A perfect base for exploring Old San Juan on foot, as we did each day and night. Would definitely stay here again, and hope to!!

<Author>kkl
<Content>You'll feel pampered My family (with 3 children) spent a week exploring Vieques- wonderful snorkeling, wild ponies, the extraordinary bioluminescent bay, miles of deserted beaches, picturesque towns, surprisingly good restaurants. But we wanted to end our Puerto Rico adventure with some city life, so we chose El Convento in Old San Juan. We came in literally dripping sand and sea water and were treated royally. Our rooms were spacious and comfortable, great bathrooms with good water pressure in the showers. Lots of little amenities, chocolates on the turned-down beds. A superb breakfast buffet, excellent coffee always available, and a complimentary wine bar in the afternoon. The kids enjoyed the little pool on the roof, and we loved the view up there. The central courtyard is beautiful, with the lights twinkling at night in the huge neem tree, hundreds of fruit bats circling. We loved exploring old San Juan on foot, the architecture, parks and squares, El Morro, the jewelry shops on Calle San Francisco. Our favorite restaurant was Bili, a few blocks from El Convento, where the food is served tapas style. It was packed with diners, the meal itself was an adventure. We hope to return to El Convento someday.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>CHARMING BUT NOT THE RITZ This is the place to stay if you are looking for charm local color in the center of Old San Juan and lots of street noice on the weekends. It is not the place to stay if you are looking for luxurious and quiet surroundings. After reading the reviews of this hotel on this website, which I usually trust, I was disappointed. My husband and I stayed at this hotel for 4 nights. The staff couldn't have been nicer --they were truly wonderful, turned themselves inside out. Our room, however left a lot to be desired. We stayed in the Casals suite, supposedly one of the nicest suites in the hotel and paid $635/night. While there were some beautiful antiques in the room, the room itself felt very old and tired, the tile on the floor must have been at least 25 years old and so dirty that the dirt was ground in. In areas around the doorways and walls, it was chipping, and looked more like a tenement. The staff at the front desk said the floor in this room was original to the hotel, which I find hard to believe, as that would make it upwards of 350 years old. There was no tile 350 years ago. The bathroom was very small, with no room to store anything, but the shower was great. Marble in the bathroom very old, with very old, dirty caulking around the tub and in between the tiles in the bath.The worst of it was Saturday night -- there was a wedding downstairs that went on to the wee hours of the morning, and it felt like the band was in our room. Impossible to sleep, then at about 5 a.m., some late-leaving drunken guests were screaming outside our window.In all fairness, I asked to see the VAnderbuilt suite. They were very nice about showing it to me and in fact, it looked much cleaner and more comfortable. It had a separate shower, and the floor was a castillo tile, so you could not see ground in dirt. Felt much more cozy and comfortable.Once of the nice things offered by the hotel is a complementary late afternoon cocktail hour -- they serve wine, cheese, crackers, coffee. They also have complementary high speed internet in the lounge. However, there is no room service at all.Bottom line is that I would not stay here again, but only because I prefer more updated, comfortable surroundings. <Author>tropicaldan
<Content>Highly Recommended ! We chose the hotel based largely on these tripadvisor guest reviews, and we were not disappointed. We stayed five nights from Nov 8th. The staff were very friendly and efficient, the hotel itself is simply beautiful, the courtyard and its magnificent tree stunning. The fifth floor room was just right, perhaps a little small but we expected that, and with a great view over the bay. No balcony, but this was compensated for by the wide and open balcony running right round the inner courtyard on each floor, and where we could sit in the evening and watch the bats in the tree or gaze over the rooftops of Old San Juan. Great stuff!The hotel organised two tours for us (we did not fancy the driving!) one to El Yunque Rain Forest and the other to the Camuy Caves, and both were very good - small personalised groups and not a huge tour bus. Saw all the hotels in the Condado, but living as we do in the Caribbean anyway, this was not our scene at all, and we are really glad we stayed at El Convento. Highly recommended.

<Author>scarlettk
<Content>Beautiful hotel, great location I was surprised at how beautiful this hotel was - because often old historic buildings converted to hotels don't really work out. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>El Convento Es Muy Bien! This hotel is outstanding! The service is top shelf quality from the minute you walk through the main door. The breakfast on the patio is a great way to start off your morning in Old San Juan. The pool is quite small, but a great place to sneak in a quick siesta. The hotel restaurants are very good, and there are several other restaurants within a short walking distance. The wine and cheese hour at 6:00 was a relaxing way to begin each evening. We got a rate of $145 per night directly off of their web site, and were upgraded to a fifth floor executive room. Our room faced the harbor, and we saw a few nice sunsets. We stayed here because of the many wonderful reviews, and are very glad we did. If you want to experience the best of Old San Juan, El Convento will deliver.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Bats, The Bats, The Bats I don't think people have mentioned how cool the bats are here. They feed every night on the little crabapple-like fruits from a 300 year old tree in the courtyard. If you find a good spot, you can sit and stay still and they will fly right up to you. Worth the price of admission just for that. Also, this hotel really isnt that expensive. $159 through expedia---, and if you factor in the free breakfast and all you can drink wine and cheese hour, you end up with a really great deal.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely Beautiful Stayed at El Convento for 3 nights before a trip to Vieques. We were SO impressed! We had heard so many bad things about San Juan that we almost did not want to stay over one night, but are so glad we did. We have both traveled extensively and been to some remote places so thought San Juan might be boring (we had heard it was a little Cancun-esque with all the hotels and cruise ships).I think staying at El Convento made all the difference. It's location - right in Old San Juan couldn't be better. [The architecture in Old SJ reminded us of Havana]. It's beautiful, and located right across from a park and adjacent to a cathedral. The streets outside are cobblestone. There were 2 weddings at the cathedral when we were there, and we could hear the music while enjoying a glass of wine from the honor bar on the veranda overlooking the park/cathedral.The room we had was somewhat small, but the ceilings were high and it served its purpose. The breakfast was hearty and we loved sitting out on the veranda in the morning with coffee (as well as evenings). The staff was great and helpful, making reservations for us a recommended restaurants, and even booking flights for us to Vieques. We ate lunch at the courtyard restaurant, and also the Paella restaurant on the second floor (forget the names), both tasty.We were debating between staying here and at the Ritz Carlton (on the beach - you know what to expect), and are SO happy we chose El Convento. I think it gave us a different perspective on San Juan!

But you will be able to convince yourself it was worth it...NOTE: If you staying at this hotel on a Monday, everything in the neighborhood is closed, and we did not find another restaurant open. Check on this if you plan to be there on a Monday.The pool is quite small, not meant for more than one couple at at time, so don't plan for laps. The outdoor whirlpool was perfectly fine.Be sure to vists the old Spanish military forts a few blocks away...Be wary of the cab drivers... Someone wanted to charge us $80.00 to drive us to the rainforests, so we skipped that.   
<Date>Jun 9, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>WONDERFUL HOTEL!! We stayed at this hotel in August, 2003 (pre/post Caribbean Cruise). This was our second time staying at the hotel since we had visited the hotel during our honeymoon in 1991. This hotel is beautiful!! We love the decorative steps, tiles, and art throughout the hotel. The breakfast buffet and evening snacks was nice. The front desk staff and bell staff were helpful. The location in Old San Juan is great. If you are traveling with children, the wonderful San Juan Children's Museum is a few steps from the front entrance. Since we stayed at the hotel twice in August, we were able to experience two very different types of room. Our first room was probably the basic room for the hotel which is very nice when compared to other San Juan hotels. The room was clean, nicely decorated and comfortable. When we returned for our second stay in August, they upgraded us to a suite which was incredible!! (at no additional cost--since this was our 2nd honeymoon and we stayed at the hotel for our 1st honeymoon--it was very thoughful). We have traveled to Europe, Africa, Asia, United States, Caribbean, Canada and South America. The suite was the most beautiful room that we have ever experienced! The suite was the size of an apartment, very spacious, beautiful decor, sunken whirlpool tub, huge closet, etc. It was the perfect way to end our San Juan trip--I still look at the photos and video of this dream suite. We look forward to returning to this outstanding hotel in the future!!

<Author>killian02
<Content>Beautiful  I had done much research - using this site and others, trying to find the best hotel for our 4-day trip to San Juan. I'm so glad I chose Hotel El Convento. It is small, charming and in a good location in Old San Juan. You can walk to everything in the area and I had no issues walking at night by myself. Found a pretty good rate on LuxRes for $195/night. Parking our rental car cost $10/night and was conveniently across the street. Driving in Old San Juan was not bad once you realize that road signs are rare - but it is easy to get your bearings. I had seriously looked at staying at the Wyndham El San Juan in Isle Verde and I went by and toured around it just to see. I'm so glad we chose El Convento - much more charm  class. El Convento is trying to install Wi-Fi  DSL but had recent issues with viruses, etc. I struggled with my laptop so much trying to connect back home, that the Operations Mgr, Oscar, kindly comped my local call chrages so I could use dialup to bypass their network.

<Author>ducatiman
<Content>Beautiful El Convento Having read other reviews we decided to stay 5 nights prior to our cruise at El Convento mainly due to its central location in the old city and the fact that is away from the crazy commercial beach front areas of Condado and Isla Verde. It was a good choice, although some kind of error in the internet booking meant we were given a queen bedded room for 3 of us. No problem, they hadn't a two bedded room available for that night and instead gave us a suite with a bed settee in the living area. (My son complained that it was most uncomfortable with a very thin mattress and had to sleep on the counterpane to pad it out a bit) They left us in the suite for 2 nights and then moved us to a double room. Both room and suite were large and comfortable and were thankfully cool, we managed to do without the aircon most of the time despite outside temps of 87f, the building has been tastefully and carefully restored, an excellent job since I belive that it was once home to the city's refuse department! It had all the facilities you would expect, although the pool could only be described as a plunge pool, but enough to cool you off and given the status of the building it couldn't be bigger anyway. A good workout room is provided with multi gym, weights, treadmill and stair walker and was very much under used, myself and my son never saw any other guests use it. Breakfast on the patio was excellent with a good selection of food available and then later in the day the same area provided an honour bar. We booked on the internet and were quoted S195 per night, the bill showed S238 per night but they quickly corrected it, taxes etc add a fair bit to the bill which finally totalled over S1200 for the 5 night stay. We enjoyed our stay although it was expensive in comparison to mainland US hotel prices but then it is not a Holiday Inn. We would definitely go back. Thankfully we had no car in San Juan and relied on our daughter and husband to drive us round. The Hotel has some space in the grounds on the cathedral opposite but if you try to park in the streets be prepared for a long tour round looking for a space.  
<Date>Apr 20, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Best of Charm, Character and Service We stayed here for 5 days in March, 2004 and found it to be one of the most charming, friendly, and comfortable of all the small hotels we've stayed at around the world. The big luxury hotels are wonderful, but just that--big. We recently stayed at the new Ritz-Carlton in MoBay and the Peninsular in Bangkok, and while both were fabulous, we found El Convento to be a pleasant change and much more relaxing. The staff was exceptionally attentive, helpful and friendly--eager to make sure our stay was what we expected from such a hotel. We were met by a bellman before we got to the front entrance who took our bags,opened up the elevator that takes you to the reception desk, and delivered the bags to our room. Reception was quick and we were not charged a deposit for either the room or safe keys. (Maybe a policy change?). We were even approached by the hotel manager who, after appropriately waiting until we activated the elevator with our room key to make certain we were guests, asked if the hotel could do anything to make our stay more enjoyable. The use of a key to operate the elevator was never inconvenient and added a high level of security and privacy, stopping outsiders and boat people from tramping through the hotel. Keep in mind that you are staying at a well known tourist attraction. The rooms were small as expected, but well appointed, clean, comfortable and charming. Our experience was much like those of the reviewers from Greenwich, CT (March 4) and San Jose, CA (March 2). And yes, as the reviewer from Orlando, FL mentioned (Feb 4), the maid staff is partial to setting the AC on ice box and the street cleaner will wake up the dead. (On the other hand, this happens only once a week and it is nice having clean streets). The hotel was exceptionally clean and the staff very responsive. When I mentioned that the maid should pull the door tight as the lock would sometimes not engage, we returned a few hours later to find a repairman had adjusted both the lock and the door closer. This hotel is in the heart of old San Juan, and unlike the big hotels on the island, gives you a feel of the city. Perhaps its nicest attraction, besides its location, is its totally open air appearance and feel. Yet you're fully secured within its old world interior as you relax on its several open air terraces. While the pool lounge chairs could be updated (they were clean and in working order) the rooftop deck is beautiful, much like a private courtyard, with good views of the sunsets. In this, I completely disagree with the reviewer from Chicago (Feb 28). No, the pool is not what you'd find on a cruise ship. This is a small, personal hotel--not the Love Boat. The included continental breakfast was more than adequate, and the fruit, rolls, several different juices and bread were fresh. The restaurants at the hotel (all independent) served well prepared and interesting food and were tasty examples of local dishes. The complemtary wine and cheese hour is well attended and offers an excellent chance to meet and talk with other guests. Excellent restaurants are within walking distance, including the well recommended and very upscale Italian restaurent across the street that (to our shock and amazement) did more than rival NY's finest in food, wine and atmosphere--and at half the price! Overall, a most relaxing and comfortable stay in the heart of what you came to see. We look forward to our return next year.  
<Date>Mar 14, 2004

<Author>Periwinkle
<Content>VERY, VERY DISAPPOINTING! We stayed at Hotel El Convento January 18, 2004 when we returned from a cruise. I completely agree with the Feb.21 review from Danbury, CT. (and we're not exaggerating when we say it's not worth the money). Where do I begin? After having a difficult time just reaching the 2nd floor check-in desk (the stairs and the elevator are accessed only by using a key), a person trying to check in does not have a key and there is very little information to help you - nor are there hotel employees around to give you direction. Thus began our initial impression of this supposedly 4 star luxury hotel. The only luxury about this place is it's high price.. Our room wasn't ready. We asked to use the washroom. The one used by hotel guests, other than their own hotel room, is off the library. There was no soap and no towels. I mentioned this to the employee at the desk. She said Oh, that will be taken care of right away. We checked back at the hotel several hours later. The room was still not ready. The restroom had towels, but no soap. There is no reason for this--especially from a highly rated one. There was smashed cigarette butts on the tile floors of the outdoor area where you eat breakfast or have the wine and cheese. The free breakfast is nothing to rave about. Yes, they serve beverages in nice containers, food is presented well....and that's the extent of it. Food is mediocre at best. And I am not a food snob....eating breakfast at a fast food restaurant is fine....so you know this is not great food! Finally our room was ready in the afternoon. We used the pool which is the size of a postage stamp. The photos of the pool are deceiving. There are very few chairs or lounges by the pool and they are dirty and need to be cleaned or better yet, replaced. Our room was nice. But we've certainly stayed in better. Our real problems began in the evening when the people in the streets began getting louder and louder. There was a all night 4 day street festival right outside the hotel. This was not told to us when we booked nor when talked to hotel employees prior to making reservations. Then around 10:30 until 1:00am a loud band played right in the hotel courtyard. My husband talked to the manager that night and the next day. They offered us a free night stay---I would never come back to this place, nor waste the money for a flight to San Juan. Unfortunately, Fodor and Frommer's book rate this place highly and fool people into staying here. When you stay here you are paying for the rich history of the hotel and not the condition it is in now nor how it is run. Please do yourself a favor and look elsewhere!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Old San Juan gem Spent a weekend at the Hotel El Convento, a small but classy hotel smack in the middle of the hustle and bustle of Old San Juan. Location is excellent but results in some interesting problems. Beware of street cleaning if your room faces the alley on the west side of the hotel. It starts at 7am on Saturday morning (which is 6am Eastern Standard time). Don't leave your window open or you'll awake to the sounds of men shouting Spanish over the roar of the pressure washing machine. If you're hoping to sleep in after a late night on Friday forget it....even with the windows CLOSED.Rooms are small but well appointed. Bathrooms are smaller. A/C typically set on ICEBOX. We reset it to 75 and the maid reset it back to ICEBOX. Good views if you face west and are on level 4 (above the buildings next door) so you can see the cruise ships depart at 10pm. Good security....key required to call elevator to ground floor. Very pretty outdoor deck area adjacent to front desk where good continental breakfast is served. Beware of lukewarm hot water with chlorine taste and similar decaf coffee. This was a problem both mornings AND at the 6-7pm wine and cheese reception (which is very well attended). Reg coffe is in electric hot pot and reliably hot.You will be charged a deposit for your keys ($25 each) and the safe lock ($75). This is refunded at check-out. Also be prepared to pay 21% tax/tourist fee each night ($80 is ALOT when added to an already expensive $400/night room). Do NOT rent a car if you plan to stay here. Traffic is a disaster and often bumper to bumper even during off peak hours. Streets are very narrow and there are pedestrians everywhere. We would recommend that you take a day tour (typically $40 to $50 per person) and HIRE that person to drive you around as needed. Much more personal and private and by the time you pay for a car rental, gas, parking, and tips, you're ahead of the game, not to mention the local knowledge and information an experienced guide can provide.Hotel pool is small, jacuzzi is lukewarm (must be the same people who make the decaf coffee) but sundeck is fabulous with excellent rooftop views. Courtyard area on first floor very charming and front entrance beautiful. Front desk personnel very helpful although area is very small and can get crowded if more than 2 people check-in with luggage.Overall, a very good hotel but in my opinion overpriced for what it offers. Still the best place to stay on Old San Juan but should cost around $250 per night rather than $400.  
<Date>Feb 4, 2004
